# Areas (Admin) - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> Configuring Areas, also referred to as BIM Areas, the Work Breakdown Structure, or the Construction Sequence, is key to being able to filter the model, create assemblies, and define work packages efficiently. Project deliverables are dependent on configured project Project Areas (Package Per Area Breakdown). The Package "Per Area Breakdown" number depends on the number of hierarchical areas defined in the project. For example, an AutoCAD model by default might only have the building as an area, whereas a Revit model might include a more granular hierarchical breakdown by Level, Scope Box, Room, etc.

---
Configuring Areas, also referred to as BIM Areas, the Work Breakdown Structure, or the Construction Sequence, is key to being able to filter the model, create assemblies, and define work packages efficiently. Project deliverables are dependent on configured project Project Areas (Package Per Area Breakdown). The Package "Per Area Breakdown" number depends on the number of hierarchical areas defined in the project. For example, an AutoCAD model by default might only have the building as an area, whereas a Revit model might include a more granular hierarchical breakdown by Level, Scope Box, Room, etc. 

-   1 [Manage Areas](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Manage-Areas)
    -   1.1 [Add Areas](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Add-Areas)
    -   1.2 [Delete Areas](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Delete-Areas)
-   2 [Edit Areas](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Edit-Areas)
    -   2.1 [Area Data Editing](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Area-Data-Editing)
-   3 [Questions](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Questions)
-   4 [Videos](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Videos)
    -   4.1 [Project Areas Overview (9:42)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742/Areas+Admin#Project-Areas-Overview-(9%3A42))

## Manage Areas

The Manage Areas button controls which areas display in the viewers.

## Add Areas

**To add Areas to the Viewers:**

1.  Publish a model and open it in the Models Viewer. Initially, there are no areas because they have not yet been selected.
    
2.  To Assign Areas, go to Projects > Areas. In this example, the model has just been published and no areas have been assigned.
    
3.  Click the **Manage Areas** button and **Select a Model**.  
    **Note: Select the model** that will be used to define areas for all models in the project.
    
4.  With the model selected, options to select Levels, Scope Boxes, and Zones displays depending on the Authoring tool. Levels must be checked.
    
5.  With Levels and Scope Boxes checked, the Levels display and are collapsed by default.
    
6.  Expand a level by clicking its **expand down arrow button** or expand all by clicking the **Expand All** button. The subareas (Ex. Scope Boxes) display. Check one or more levels (Ex. L01) and Scope Boxes (Ex. OA1, etc.) that will become areas in the Viewer. All parts in these areas will be assigned to the areas.
    
7.  To expedite the selection of areas, enter a value in the **Search** text box and then click the **Check Matches** button. Use the **Uncheck Matches** to uncheck any selected areas.
    
8.  Before clicking update, in this example, this level and these scope boxes have been selected.
    
9.  Click the **Update** button.
    
10.  The Projects > Areas page refreshes:
    
    1.  The selected Levels and Scope boxes populate the data table.
        
    2.  The Models Viewer is updated to display the selected Areas. Any deselected areas would be removed from the Models Viewer.
        
    3.  The **Stratus.Part.BIMArea** property for each part in the area is now populated with the area.
        
    4.  The **Assign Parts** buttons, **Assign Parts (All Models)** and **Assign Unassigned Parts (All Models)** are highlighted yellow.
        

## Delete Areas

**To delete Areas from the Viewers:**

1.  In this example, the data table has been edited and two Abbreviations have been added.
    
2.  Click the **Manage Areas** button and expand the currently selected level (Ex. L01). The scope boxes areas will display.
    
3.  Uncheck several scope box areas like these 4 scope boxes. **Note**: The SC-OB2 Abbreviation was previously entered in the data table for this scope box area.
    
4.  Click **Update**.
    
    1.  The **Project Areas** pages displays:
        
        1.  The unchecked scope box areas are removed from the data table.
            
        2.  Since the row (Area) OB2 was deleted, the Abbreviation (Ex. SC-OB2) for that row has also been deleted.
            
        3.  The row (Area) OA1 is still selected, therefore, the Abbreviation (Ex. SC-OA1) remains.
            
        4.  The **Assign Parts** buttons are highlighted yellow.
            
    2.  In the **Models Viewer**:
        
        1.  The unchecked scope box areas (Ex. OB1, etc.) are deleted from the viewer.
            
        2.  For the deleted areas, the Stratus.Part.BIMArea property value has been deleted.
            

## Edit Areas

## Area Data Editing

1.  **Edit Row (Area) Data** - Double-click a row to edit the row data.
    
2.  **Name** - The imported areas will display in a tree structure under the Name column. The name of each Level, Scope Box, etc. will display. Names are not editable, but the Sort order is editable. See the Sort by Name and Sort by Elevation options below.
    
3.  **Delete** - Select a row and then click **Delete** to delete the row.
    
    1.  The Delete Area prompt will display.
        
    2.  Click **OK**. The area will be deleted from the viewers and the Area data table.
        
    3.  **Note**: To add the area back into the viewers, click **Manage Areas,** check the area, and then on the Areas page, click the **Assign Parts (All Models)** button. Otherwise, the area will not display in the viewer.
        
4.  **Save** \- Select an area, edit a cell value (Ex. Abbreviation, Elevation, Range). The Save button is enabled. Click the **Save** button, or, click anywhere on the page and the value will be saved.
    
5.  **Cancel** \- Select an area, edit a cell value (Ex. Abbreviation, Elevation, Range). The Cancel button is enabled. Click the **Cancel** button and the value will be cancelled.
    
6.  **Expand All** - By default, all areas are expanded. Use the Expand All button to expand the areas after they have been collapsed.
    
7.  **Collapse All** - Use the Collapse All button to collapse all areas to the highest tree branch, usually the model. Expand the model to view collapsed Levels.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/44341d6c-23a8-4837-ae07-0951fb9963ef)
    
8.  **Add Row Below** - The **Add Row Below** button is intended for those projects where the admin wants to manually build a hierarchy of areas and manually choose the relationships between them (Ex. grid areas, scope boxes, etc.). The **Add Row Below** button enables you to add an area row below the selected area. When clicked, a copy of the selected row will be add to the data grid. Edit the row as needed. **Note**: In one of the Viewers, Filter by Area and the newly added area row will display. It does not yet have any parts associated with it. See the Graphical Selector section below. 
    
9.  **Add Row Child** - The **Add Row Child** button is intended for those projects where the admin wants to manually build a hierarchy of areas and manually choose the relationships between them (Ex. grid areas, scope boxes, etc.). Click the **Add Row Child** button to add an indented row (child) to the selected row. The selected row becomes a parent row that can be expanded and collapsed. Edit the row as needed. **Note**: In one of the Viewers, Filter by Area and the newly added area row will display. It does not yet have any parts associated with it. See the Graphical Selector section below.
    
10.  **Assign Parts (All Models)** - The **Assign Parts (All Models)** is enabled after any change is made to the data table and when a model is published. Click the **Assign Parts (All Models)** button when the changes should be applied to all parts.
    
    1.  For example, if **Abbreviations** have been added to one or more rows, then the STRATUS.Part.BIMAbbreviation property will be added to all parts in the specified area.
        
11.  **Assign Unassigned Parts (All Models)** - The **Assign Unassigned Parts (All Models)** button is enabled after any change is made to the data table and when a model is published. The **Assign Unassigned Parts (All Models)** button can be clicked during subsequent model publishes to ensure that parts are correctly assigned to new model areas and that existing parts that have already been assigned are not modified.
    
12.  **Arrows** 
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/f6a34a61-1b04-4880-a835-e7fb6c2794bc)
    
    1.  **Up** - Moves the selected row up.
        
    2.  **Down** - Moves the selected row down.
        
    3.  **Left** - Outdents the selected row so that a child row is at the same level as a parent.
        
    4.  **Right** - Indents the selected row so that the row becomes a child of the row above.
        
13.  **Sort by Name** - Click **Sort by Name** to sort the rows by the Name column in alphabetic order.  
    **Note**: The row order on the Areas page will drive the row order on the Projects > Deliverables page. 
    
14.  **Sort by Elevation** \- Click **Sort by Elevation** to sort the rows by the Elevation column (lowest to highest).  
    **Note**: The row order on the Areas page will drive the row order on the Projects > Deliverables page. 
    
15.  **Graphical Selector** - By default, when the model includes Levels, Scope Boxes, Zones, Rooms, and Spaces, those will be automatically be matched up when the Import as Areas button is clicked (above).  The Graphical Selector can be used to override or redefine areas in the model that will be assigned to the selected row area.  
    
    1.  The **Graphical Selector** is accessed by double-clicking any area row and clicking the **Graphical Selector** button in the Contents column.  The Select Regions for Area dialog will display. In this example, the region displays and since Scope Boxes were defined in the model, the SB (Scope Box) button is automatically selected, and the row area's scope box checkbox is selected.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/b9503460-b2df-4312-813c-309064ff0314)
        
        1.  **Clear Area** - The Clear Area button (not displayed) can be used to clear out previous data and selections enabling the user to check areas.
            
    2.  **Display grid** - To override default area settings, click the **Display grid** button to display grid cells with a checkbox in the center. Grids will display if the model includes Display Grids. By clicking a checkbox, any part whose centroid is within the grid cell will be assigned to the selected area.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/993a492a-5d45-48b5-9239-5208722be3d4)
        
        1.  Click **Done**. The Areas table will refresh and the Contents of the select row will update with the number of grid cells that are included in the area.
            
        2.  Since the Area data has been edited, the **Assign Unassigned Parts (All Models)** button will highlight yellow indicating that the parts have not yet been assigned to the area. Click the **Assign Unassigned Parts (All Models)** button to assign all parts in the model to the areas noted on the Areas page.
            
    3.  **RM** - Click the RM button to manually select Room regions for the area of the selected row.
        
    4.  **SM** - Click the SB button to manually select Scope Box regions for the area of the selected row. **Note**: If an assembly is inside two scope boxes, all assembly parts will be assigned to the area where the assembly centroid is located. 
        
    5.  **SP** - Click the SP button to manually select Space regions for the area of the selected row.
        
    6.  **Grid Line Note**: For Grid Lines to display properly:
        
        1.  In the model, finalize any name changes to the grid lines. Grid line definitions for a model are purged and reloaded on every model publish. If a grid line name changes, links to those names are broken in Stratus.
            
        2.  If the model is republished with updated grid line names:
            
            1.  Use the **Clear Area** button to clear all grid cell associations to project areas and remove all part area associations.
                
            2.  Using the areas tools, rebuild the grid cell associations so that the project areas are linked to the correct grid line names and the parts are associated with the correct areas. You can assign the grid cells at all levels of the project area tree structure. Do this for several areas and auto-assign parts. Make sure these associations are correct using the Models > Viewer > Display Modes > Areas tab.
                
16.  **Abbreviation** - Manually enter an abbreviation for each row if you want Stratus to automatically use the Area Abbreviation field as part of your assembly or package naming scheme under Admin > Company > Naming Conventions. See the [**Naming and Numbering (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913") article for more information. Since area abbreviations are used within the name of an assembly or package, you'll want to standardize the naming scheme and keep them short.
    
17.  **Elevation** - While you can edit the elevation, this elevation comes from the model so won't likely need to be changed.
    
18.  **Range Bottom Offset and Range Top Offset** - The Range Bottom and Range Top settings tell Stratus which parts in the Z will be included in the area. 
    
    1.  For example, in the Models > Viewer, you may filter to an area that should include anchors, but it doesn't. This is because the anchor centroid is outside of the Range Bottom or Range Top setting.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/702921da-46a7-4ca6-bd2a-cf3f9ec5d8c1)
        
    2.  In this example, I'll enter -5" as the Range Bottom Offset for all of the Roof areas, and, to "offset" this I'll enter -5" as the Range Top Offset for all of the Level 1 areas.
        
    3.  If any changes are made, click the **Assign Parts (All Models)** button to assign parts to the area. 
        
    4.  Once the Models > Viewer is refreshed, Filter to the Areas (Roof), the anchors now display.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/0f41ff72-fb49-4a1f-a560-b25f15607c50)
        
19.  **Code** - The Code represents a sub-string for cost coding. The Code will be used in the future but is not currently an active feature.
    
20.  **Color** - Row colors display in the Viewers under Display Modes > Areas. 
    

## Questions

**Q:** If after defining project areas the model is republished, will project areas be lost.  
**A:** No, republishing the model does not overwrite or delete project areas defined in Stratus. In fact, if new parts are added to an area in the model, they will be included in the defined area in Stratus. And, if parts are removed from the model, they will also be removed from Stratus.

**Q:** Are project areas imported back into the model or drawing?  
**A:** No. A Project Area is a Stratus only definition. It really does not need to be part of the model or drawing data.

**Q:** I have already set project areas by clicking the Assign Parts button. If the model is republished, will the new parts added to the model be assigned the correct project area?  
**A:** Yes, the Part Property = Stratus.Part.BIMArea will be assigned the correct area based on the project area assignments.

## Videos

## Project Areas Overview (9:42)

This is an older video that includes the no longer used Import Areas option which has been replaced with the Manage Areas option. It does a nice job demonstrating how to the Range Bottom and Range Top data values can be used.

1.  How to how to import and configure areas from a Revit model or CADmep drawing.
    
2.  How to use the Graphical Selector to manually add quadrants to an area.
    
3.  How to Assign areas to parts.
    
4.  How to auto-name a spool with an Area abbreviation.
    
5.  How to isolate areas to create assemblies or packages.

# Assemblies Dashboard - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> From this tab, you can access the Assemblies Dashboard.

---
From this tab, you can access the Assemblies Dashboard.

-   1[Project Role Permissions](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8912924/Assemblies+Dashboard#AssembliesDashboard-ProjectRolePermissions)
-   2[Summary](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8912924/Assemblies+Dashboard#AssembliesDashboard-Summary)
-   3[In-Grid Editing](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8912924/Assemblies+Dashboard#AssembliesDashboard-In-GridEditing)
    -   3.1[Import CSV](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8912924/Assemblies+Dashboard#AssembliesDashboard-ImportCSV)

## Project Role Permissions

Under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Assemblies > Dashboard, the following permissions now display.

![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-24_16-51-17.png?version=1&modificationDate=1656107478127&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=400&height=385)

-   **Attachments** \- When checked the project role can add an attachment to an assembly.
    
-   **Delete** - When checked the project role can view the Delete column and delete assemblies.
    
-   **Edit Assembly Properties** - When checked the project role can edit the Status of the assembly and any editable properties in custom reports.
    
-   **Modify Packages** - When checked the project role can add/remove assemblies to/from a package.
    
-   **View** \- When checked the project role can view the Assemblies > Dashboard, including Attachments.
    

## Summary

The Assemblies Dashboard displays assemblies filtered by Project, Model, Division, Package, and Status.  The list can be further filtered by column filters or sort options. Each assembly displays information including a link to packages that contain the assembly. Each assembly can be expanded to display its child parts.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-23-49.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696537431378&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)

1.  **Dashboard or Viewer default** - Hover over the Dashboard or Viewer tab and click the checkbox to set it as the default tab when the Assemblies button is clicked.
2.  **Project** - Select one project or the ALL PROJECTS option. **Note**: Loading 100 assemblies will take about 15 seconds. 
    
3.  **Model** - Select one model or the ALL MODELS option within the selected project. **Note**: Loading 100 assemblies will take about 15 seconds. 
    
4.  **Division** - Filter the list to one or ALL Divisions.
    
5.  **Package** - Filter the list to one package or Unspecified for all packages.
    
6.  **Status** - Filter the list to one or more Tracking Statuses.
7.  **Import CSV** - Import assembly row data from a CSV file. 
8.  **Clear Cached Calculated Field Values and Reload Data Table** button - When User A loads the Assemblies Dashboard page for the first time, if there are any calculated fields in the report, they are cached. As a result, the next time any user loads the page the cached data will be retrieved faster than the original load. Cached data is purged and cached either manually using the **Clear Cached Calculated Field Values and Reload Data Table** button or automatically. Note: The same button is also implemented on the Packages Dashboard. 
    
    Assemblies Dashboard calculated cached values are automatically purged when:
    
    -   any type of assembly modification is made such as editing parts in the assembly
        
    -   using a field that is a total value from all parts in the assembly
        
    -   a Field references a Part property or another Field value, and they are modified
        
9.  **Assembly Report** - The Default Assembly Report includes the fields and functionality described below. Users can configure a custom assembly report. For the custom assembly report to display in the drop-down list, its Item Type = Assembly and the checkbox for Assemblies Dashboard must be checked. See the **[Reports (Admin)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin)** article for more information.
    
    1.  **Multiple Entry Selection and Action** - Multiple entries (rows) can be selected and then an action can be taken on those entries (Ex. Update Tracking Status, edit an editable field, and Delete). See the **[Multiple Entry Selection and Action FAQ](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1963720705/Multiple+Entry+Selection+and+Action)** for more information and examples.
    2.  **Expand / Collapse** \- Expand to view the assembly’s parts. Collapse to hide the assembly’s parts.
        
    3.  **Type** - The assembly type is detected as one of the following:
        1.  **Assembly** - if AssemblyType.RevitAssembly = Assembly, used with Revit or unspecified models
        2.  **Conduit** - if AssemblyType.RevitCustomMark = Conduit, used for models that include Bendworks items
        3.  **Custom** - if AssemblyType.RevitParameter = Custom
        4.  **Family** - if AssemblyType.RevitNestedFamily = Family
        5.  **Hanger** - if AssemblyType.RevitHanger = Hanger, used for models that include HangerWorks items
        6.  **Spool** - if AssemblyType.CADmepSpool = Spool, used with AutoCAD models
        7.  **Unspecified** - if AssemblyType.Unspecified = Unspecified
    4.  **Assembly Name** - The Assembly Name column displays the assembly name, a link to edit the assembly name, and a link to the Assemblies > Viewer tab.  For edit assembly name permission, check **Edit Assembly Properties** under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Assemblies > Dashboard. 
        
        1.  **Assembly Name** - Displays the assembly name. 
            
        2.  **Edit** - Click the assembly name to edit the name.  
            ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2022-6-6_16-26-35.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654550796386&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
        3.  **Assembly Viewer Link** - Click the assembly link icon to open the assembly in the user's default Assemblies tab. 
            
    5.  **Packages** - The Packages column displays the name(s) of the package(s) that contain the assembly, an Add/Remove option, and a link to the package’s viewer.  For Package edit permission, check **Modify Packages** under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Assemblies > Dashboard. 
        
        1.  **Packages names** - If the assembly is included in one or more packages, the package(s) name(s) will display.
            
        2.  **Package open** - To open the package in a separate window, click the link icon associated with the package, and the user’s default Packages tab will open.
            
        3.  **Add/Remove Assembly To/From Package** - Click any package name to display the Packages dialog to add the assembly to a different package or remove the assembly from a package.
            
            1.  **Add** - To add the assembly to a package, click the drop-down and select the package. Packages that an assembly cannot be added to due to rules (Ex. Package must be in a "Can Package" tracking status or the assembly can only be added to a Package in a Package Category once) are disabled.  
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-13_9-42-15.png?version=1&modificationDate=1655131337496&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=700&height=385)
                
            2.  **Remove** - To remove the assembly from a package, click the x associated with the package.  
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-6_16-22-9.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654550530923&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=511&height=250)
                
            3.  After the Packages dialog save button is clicked, a message similar to the following will display letting you know the name of the assembly(s) and the name of the package(s) impacted by the modification.  
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2022-6-15_15-52-6.png?version=1&modificationDate=1655326327847&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
                
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2022-6-15_15-53-11.png?version=1&modificationDate=1655326392913&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
                
            4.  Assemblies > Dashboard permission are controlled under Admin > Company Project Roles > Modify Packages.   
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-15_15-54-39.png?version=1&modificationDate=1655326480215&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=423&height=250)
                1.  **Attachments** \- When checked the project role can add an attachment to an assembly.
                    
                2.  **Delete** - When checked the project role can view the Delete column and delete assemblies.
                    
                3.  **Edit Assembly Properties** - When checked the project role can edit the Status of the assembly and any editable properties in custom reports.
                    
                4.  **Modify Packages** - When checked the project role can add/remove assemblies to/from a package.
                    
                5.  **View** \- When checked the project role can view the Assemblies > Dashboard, including Attachments.
                    
        4.  **Instance** - The Instance field for HangerWorks hangers, when populated, indicates the number of instances of a certain assembly based on the "Prefab Id" parameter. 
        5.  **Parts** \- Displays the number of parts included in the assembly.
            
        6.  **Hours** \- Displays the number of actual assembly hours entered while updating the assembly’s tracking status. Actual hours can be manually entered while using the Update Tracking Status dialog. This prompt displays:
            
            1.  On the Assemblies > Dashboard tab when the tracking Status is updated within the Assembly Report.
                
            2.  On the Assemblies > Viewer tab when the tracking Status is updated.
            3.  On the Models > Viewer > Actions > Tracking tab when an assembly is selected.
            4.  On the Packages > Viewer > Actions > Tracking tab when an assembly is selected.  
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-6_16-39-31.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654551572581&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=294&height=250)
                
        7.  **Status** \- The Status column displays the tracking status of the assembly. To modify the Status:
            
            1.  Click the link to display the **Update Assembly Tracking Status** prompt.  
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-10_14-20-32.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654888833695&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=292&height=250)
                
            2.  Select a Status and click **Update**. Optionally, select a Division, Cost Type, enter a Comment, or attach a file.
        8.  **User** \- Displays the name of the user who last updated the assembly’s tracking status.
            
        9.  **Date-Time** - Displays the date-time the assembly’s tracking status was last updated.
            
        10.  **Attachments **(Displays on custom report too)**** \- Click the assembly’s **Upload Attachment** button to attach a file to the assembly.  For attach a file permission, check **Attachments** under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Assemblies > Dashboard. 
            
            1.  Click the assembly's **Upload Attachment** ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2020-1-22_9-14-49.png?version=1&modificationDate=1579706507306&cacheVersion=1&api=v2) button to locate and upload a part attachment.
            2.  Once a file is attached the **Open Attachments**![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2019-10-1_10-14-45.png?version=1&modificationDate=1579706507434&cacheVersion=1&api=v2) button will display and can be clicked to open the attachment. The attachment can also be opened under the Assemblies > Viewer > Attachments tab.
        11.  **Delete** **(Displays on custom report too)** - Click the **Delete** button to be prompted to delete the assembly. The parts will be disassociated from the assembly but will retain their current tracking status.  For Delete assembly permission, check **Delete** under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Assemblies > Dashboard.
            
        12.  **Delete** **(Displays on custom report too)** \- Assemblies whose tracking status has the "Can Assemble" checkbox checked under Admin > Company > Tracking Statuses can be deleted. When an assembly cannot be deleted, these options will not display.  
            1.  **Delete** - Assemblies that have been deleted in STRATUS are not “hard deleted” from the STRATUS database until the model is re-published from Revit or AutoCAD back into STRATUS.  Scenarios like the following are handled. Be sure to understand the Import message that displays following an import.
                1.  Creating a new STRATUS assembly with the same name as one just deleted and with different parts than the deleted assembly.
                2.  Creating a new assembly with the deleted assembly’s name and with a subset of the deleted assembly’s parts.
                3.  Note: Revit and AutoCAD, unlike STRATUS, do not save changes until you explicitly save them or run a publish. Therefore, if during a STRATUS Import, Revit or AutoCAD crashes, change since the last save will be lost. In addition, the next Import will re-do whatever is different in STRATUS from that point rather than from the point of your previous unsaved imports.
        13.  **Show** - Show All entries or limit to a set number of rows to improve performance.
        14.  **CSV | Excel** - Download the data table list as a CSV or Excel file format.
        15.  **Search** - Filter the list by searching for specific characters.
        16.  **Sort** \- The list of assemblies can be sorted by Assembly Name, Packages, Parts, Hours, Status, User, or Date-Time.
            
        17.  **Filter** - The list of assemblies can be filtered by Packages, Parts, Hours, Status, User, and Date-Time. 
            1.  **Status Filter Note** - In the Status filter, only tracking Statuses where "Can Assemble" and "Applies to Assembly"  are checked will display in the list.
            2.  **Date-Time Note:** The Date-Time or any date column will display the From and To date range dialog.  
                ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2022-6-7_15-16-22.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654632983400&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
                1.  Click the date value to edit the date.  
                    ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-7_15-18-29.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654633110724&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=253&height=250)
                2.  Click the x to clear the date.   
                    ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2022-6-7_15-33-37.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654634018581&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
10.  **Part Report** - The Default Part Report includes the following fields and functionality. Users can configure a custom part report. The custom part report will display in the Part Report drop-down when the report Item Type = Part and the checkbox for Assemblies Dashboard is checked.
    
    1.  **Quantity (Displays on custom report too)** - Displays the quantity of parts in the assembly. Since the default report does not include any merge or totaling options, the quantity will always be 1.
        
    2.  **Description** \- Displays the part description.
        
    3.  **Assembly Name** - Displays the name of the assembly for which the part is included.
        
    4.  **Hours** \- Displays the number of actual part Hours entered while updating the part’s tracking status. Actual hours can be manually entered during the Update Tracking Status prompt. This prompt displays:
        
        1.  On the Assemblies > Dashboard tab when the tracking Status is updated within the Assembly Report.
            
        2.  On the Assemblies > Viewer tab when the tracking Status is updated.
        3.  On the Models > Viewer > Actions > Tracking tab when an assembly is selected.
        4.  On the Packages > Viewer > Actions > Tracking tab when an assembly is selected.  
            ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-6_16-40-50.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654551651504&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=296&height=250)
            
    5.  **Status** \- Status includes the part's current tracking Status name and color. Click the Status name to change the tracking status with the **Update Part Tracking Status** prompt (see above).
        
        1.  **Note**:  If the tracking status for parts in an assembly are updated, the assembly status will display the lowest STRATUS.Part.TrackingStatusIndex number among its associated parts. For example, if there are 5 parts in an assembly where the tracking status for 1 part is Issued for Fabrication (STRATUS.Part.TrackingStatusIndex = 6) and 4 parts are Cut (STRATUS.Part.TrackingStatusIndex = 7), then the assembly tracking status will be Issued for Fabrication.
            
    6.  **Attachments **(Displays on custom report too)**** \- For attach a file permission, check **Attachments** under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Assemblies > Dashboard.
        1.  Click the part's **Upload Attachment** ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2020-1-22_9-14-49.png?version=1&modificationDate=1579706507306&cacheVersion=1&api=v2) button to locate and upload a part attachment.
        2.  Once a file is attached the **Open Attachments**![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2019-10-1_10-14-45.png?version=1&modificationDate=1579706507434&cacheVersion=1&api=v2) button will display and can be clicked to open the attachment.
        3.  Delete a part's attachment under Assemblies Viewer > Attachments.
    7.  **Search** - Filter the list by searching for specific characters.
    8.  **Sort** - The list of parts can be sorted by Description, Assembly Name, Hours, and Status.
        
    9.  **Filter** \- The list of parts can be filtered by Description, Assembly Name, Hours, or Status. When set, a filter is used until the user changes it. In this example, the parts table is filtered by Status = Issue for Fabrication. Notice that assembly WS-6-ROOF-0003 (bottom assembly) does not have any parts in this tracking status so only the filter displays.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2022-6-6_17-4-31.png?version=1&modificationDate=1654553074423&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=1000&height=339)
        

## In-Grid Editing

In-Grid editing on the Assemblies Dashboard makes editing faster.

![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/8912924/image2018-11-15_8-35-57.png?version=1&modificationDate=1542292560395&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=624&height=170)

## Import CSV

1.  **Download the CSV file** - Click the **CSV** button. The CSV is downloaded and can be opened.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-26-11.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696537573783&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
2.  **Edit Existing Data and Import** - To edit existing assemblies for import, edit any data value except Id. All Assembly Names must be unique. When done Click the **Import CSV** button.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-33-33.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696538015835&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
    
3.  **Add a New Row** - To add a new row:
    
    1.  Add the data, make sure the Assembly Names are unique, and leave the Id blank.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-38-5.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696538287340&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
        
    2.  Click **Import CSV**. The new rows will display.
        
        ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-39-29.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696538371503&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
4.  Click the **CSV** button to export the table and the new rows will have been assigned an Id.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-40-56.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696538458049&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
    
5.  **Duplicate Id** - Copy a row, change the Name to a unique value, but duplicate an Id.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-42-43.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696538565095&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
    
    1.  The row will be imported, however it will replace the row that previously had the Id.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_15-45-49.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696538751630&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)
        
    2.  After clicking CSV to export, you’ll see that TA-HNG-000111111 which had the duplicate Id was overwritten to TA-HNG-000111122 and takes over the Id.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/8912924/image2023-10-5_16-4-1.png?version=1&modificationDate=1696539843510&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)

# Assemblies Viewer - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Assemblies > Viewer tab displays an assembly. An assembly displays when a users clicks a link from another page like a dashboard or by using the assembly filter tools (Ex. Project, Model, Package, Assembly).  The assembly’s Status, Division, Comment, Hours, and Cost Type can be updated. The 3D viewer section includes the STRATUS Toolbar. The detailed content section, includes tabs for Parts, STRATUS Sheet, CAD Sheet, Notes, Attachments, Tracking, and Tasks.

---
The Assemblies > Viewer tab displays an assembly. An assembly displays when a users clicks a link from another page like a dashboard or by using the assembly filter tools (Ex. Project, Model, Package, Assembly). The assembly’s Status, Division, Comment, Hours, and Cost Type can be updated. The 3D viewer section includes the STRATUS Toolbar. The detailed content section, includes tabs for Parts, STRATUS Sheet, CAD Sheet, Notes, Attachments, Tracking, and Tasks.

-   1 [Open Assembly](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly)
    -   1.1 [Open Assembly from the Models Viewer](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-from-the-Models-Viewer)
    -   1.2 [Open Assembly from the Packages > Viewer](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-from-the-Packages-%3E-Viewer)
    -   1.3 [Open Assembly from the STRATUS Home Page](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-from-the-STRATUS-Home-Page)
    -   1.4 [Open Assembly from the Assemblies > Dashboard](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-from-the-Assemblies-%3E-Dashboard)
    -   1.5 [Open Assembly by Scanning QR Code with Handheld Scanner](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-by-Scanning-QR-Code-with-Handheld-Scanner)
    -   1.6 [Open Assembly by Scanning QR Code with the Tablet’s Camera](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-by-Scanning-QR-Code-with-the-Tablet%E2%80%99s-Camera)
    -   1.7 [Open Assembly by Scanning to the Assembly QR Code Scanned Page](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-by-Scanning-to-the-Assembly-QR-Code-Scanned-Page)
    -   1.8 [Open Assembly from the Containers > Dashboard](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Open-Assembly-from-the-Containers-%3E-Dashboard)

-   4 [3D Viewer - Settings](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#3D-Viewer---Settings)
-   5 [3D Viewer Search for Parts](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#3D-Viewer-Search-for-Parts)
-   6 [3D Viewer - Rename Assembly](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#3D-Viewer---Rename-Assembly)
-   7 [3D Viewer - STRATUS Toolbar](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#3D-Viewer---STRATUS-Toolbar) 
    -   7.1 [Display Modes](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Display-Modes)
    -   7.2 [Filters](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Filters)
    -   7.3 [Grid Offset Measurement](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Grid-Offset-Measurement)
    -   7.4 [Display Grid](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Display-Grid)
    -   7.5 [Properties](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Properties)
    -   7.6 [Display Tags and Item Numbers Toolbar](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Display-Tags-and-Item-Numbers-Toolbar)
        -   7.6.1 [Project Roles](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Project-Roles)
        -   7.6.2 [Display Tags and Item Numbers Toolbar](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Display-Tags-and-Item-Numbers-Toolbar.1)
        -   7.6.3 [Renumber Parts (Stratus.Part.Number)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Renumber-Parts-(Stratus.Part.Number))
