# Companies - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Companies tab displays information about your STRATUS subscription.

---
The Companies tab displays information about your STRATUS subscription.

-   1 [Companies](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1953857908/Companies#Companies)
    -   1.1 [Override Project Roles for Testing](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1953857908/Companies#Override-Project-Roles-for-Testing)

## Companies

The Companies table lists the name of the companies that you have been given access to, the type of BIM 360 account, the type of Subscription, the end date of the Subscription, and for those who have the Project Admin Role, an Override Project Roles for Testing option.

![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/0e778760-e118-4629-8a62-b415c83f32f3#media-blob-url=true&id=28860e9a-62a0-448b-84f5-57a9c1a1bd18&collection=contentId-1953857908&contextId=1953857908&mimeType=image%2Fpng&name=image-20220819-200528.png&size=56319&width=1367&height=358&alt=)

## Override Project Roles for Testing

For those who have the Project Admin Role under Admin > Project, Team, use the **Override Project Roles for Testing** option to change your Project Role so that you can experience STRATUS the way a user with that Project Role sees it.

To use the **Override Project Roles for Testing** option:

1.  Click your badge icon in the top right corner, then click Account Settings > Companies.
    
2.  For the selected company, use the **Override Project Roles for Testing** drop-down to change your project role within that company. These roles are the ones setup under Admin > Company > Project Roles.
    
3.  Once you’ve changed the project role, the page will refresh and the red triangle icon will display.
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/5021c728-4d60-4050-a1fa-7232dfad45e5#media-blob-url=true&id=cb2663ff-068d-4d6e-999d-777a706d8fae&collection=contentId-1953857908&contextId=1953857908&mimeType=image%2Fpng&name=image-20220819-200934.png&size=54710&width=919&height=244&alt=)
    
4.  From here you can navigate STRATUS as that project role.
    
5.  When done, return to Account Settings > Companies and select the blank Override Project Roles for Testing option to have your project role again.

# Containers Assign - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Container feature provides the ability to select Containers, add items (Parts, Assemblies, Packages, Shop Items, and other Containers) to the Container, and print a Container label or a Container Details report. Once a label or report that includes a QR Code is printed, it can be scanned to display a landing page where Tracking status changes can be made to a container that trickle down to all their contents. See the Containers (Admin) article for more information on how to configure containers.

---
The Container feature provides the ability to select Containers, add items (Parts, Assemblies, Packages, Shop Items, and other Containers) to the Container, and print a Container label or a Container Details report. Once a label or report that includes a QR Code is printed, it can be scanned to display a landing page where Tracking status changes can be made to a container that trickle down to all their contents. See the [**Containers (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/246317057 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/246317057") article for more information on how to configure containers.

-   1 [Add Items to a Container](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Add-Items-to-a-Container)
    -   1.1 [Add Items to Container - Manual](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Add-Items-to-Container---Manual)
    -   1.2 [Add Items to Container - Hand Scanner](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Add-Items-to-Container---Hand-Scanner)
        -   1.2.1 [(Video 1:25)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#(Video-1%3A25))
        -   1.2.2 [Scan Errors](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Scan-Errors)
    -   1.3 [Add Items to Container - Tablet or Phone Camera Scanner](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Add-Items-to-Container---Tablet-or-Phone-Camera-Scanner)
-   2 [Move Items to a Different Container](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Move-Items-to-a-Different-Container)
    -   2.1 [Move Items to a Different Container - Manual](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Move-Items-to-a-Different-Container---Manual)
    -   2.2 [Move Items to a Different Container - Scan](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Move-Items-to-a-Different-Container---Scan)
-   3 [Container Tracking Log Entry](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Container-Tracking-Log-Entry)
-   4 [Add Container A to Container B (Sub-container)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Add-Container-A-to-Container-B-(Sub-container))
-   5 [Reports](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Reports)
    -   5.1 [Container](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Container)
    -   5.2 [Container Details](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Container-Details)
    -   5.3 [Container Part, Assembly, or Package Report](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Container-Part%2C-Assembly%2C-or-Package-Report)
    -   5.4 [Print Container Label](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Print-Container-Label)
-   6 [Scan and Report Mode](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Scan-and-Report-Mode)
-   7 [Scan the Container QR Code](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Scan-the-Container-QR-Code)
-   8 [Videos](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Videos)
    -   8.1 [Stratus 09/10/2020 Implementation Webinar \- Containers 21:55](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Stratus-09%2F10%2F2020-Implementation-Webinar---Containers-21%3A55)
    -   8.2 [Stratus 06-20-19 Implementation Webinar (Containers 27:44)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151/Containers+Assign#Stratus-06-20-19-Implementation-Webinar-(Containers-27%3A44))

## Add Items to a Container

The Containers page provides several ways to select and add items to a container:

![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/84a0b5ab-fb34-41cc-b1e4-144262e51f0b)

1.  **Manual** - A container can be manually selected. See the [**Manually Add Items to Container**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers#HowtoManuallyAddItemstoContainer "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers#HowtoManuallyAddItemstoContainer") section for more information.
    
2.  **Hand Scanner** - Use a hand scanner to scan the container's QR Code. See the [**Work with Containers Using a Hand Scanner**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers#HowtoWorkwithContainersUsingaHandScanner "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers#HowtoWorkwithContainersUsingaHandScanner") section for more information.
    
3.  **Tablet or Phone Camera Scan** - Use a Tablet or Phone Camera scanner to scan the container's QR Code. See the [**Work with Containers Using a Tablet or Phone Camera Scan**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers#HowtoWorkwithContainersUsingaTabletorPhoneCameraScan "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers#HowtoWorkwithContainersUsingaTabletorPhoneCameraScan") section for more information.
    
4.  **Package Categories > Use Containers** - A company doesn't want every package to be exposed to a Container. Under Admin > Company > [**Package Categories**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351"), uncheck the **Use Containers** checkbox so that these packages don’t display in the Containers drop-down.
    

## Add Items to Container - Manual

**To select and manually add items to a container:**

1.  Under Containers > Assign, click the **Container** drop-down.
    
2.  Select a target container. If the list of containers is long, you can limit the list of Containers by selecting the container type (Area, Basket, etc.) and a list of those container types will display.  
    
3.  With the container selected the Containers page is ready for you to manually add items to the container.
    
4.  **Exclude Contained items** - Determine whether or not you want to **Exclude Contained items** which will exclude items from the Manual Selection list if the item is contained in any container. Checking this option is a device-specific setting and will be cleared when the user unchecks the setting or when the browser cache is cleared.
    
    1.  **Unchecked (Default)** - When Unchecked, the default behavior of adding/removing items to/from the Contents of the container is that packages, assemblies, parts, and containers that have been added to the currently selected container are filtered out of the lists on the left under Manual Selection.
        
    2.  **Checked** - When checked:
        
        1.  The setting will be saved to the device's local storage.
            
        2.  The Manual Selection drop-down lists will now exclude any items that are included in any Container. In this example, parts of of Package REV-DIM-0001 have been added to Truck B.
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/3ba70e02-9896-42c9-a782-8a03738f57c8)
            
        3.  Switch to a different Container (Ex. Truck D). Since the Package still includes items that are not yet in a container, the package will still display, but the items that are included in a different container (Ex. Truck B) do not display in the list.
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/dbc929f1-5843-4178-8e2e-9a3f19f7e209)
            
5.  To add items like a part, assembly, package, or shop item to the selected container, under the Manual Selection section, identify the Project, Model, Container, and or Item that will be added to the container. 
    
6.  As you add items to the Container, the Contents will grow.
    
7.  Assembly parts can be expanded and contracted by clicking the **expander icon**
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/8fbd72a5-65a0-43d9-b633-5b195d0e590a)
    
    **.**  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/2944dfda-ca30-4315-a95e-f6f8e4d3d54b)
    
8.  **To Remove Items from the Contents of a Container**, either:
    
    1.  Click the **Remove** button to remove an individual item. After all individual items have been removed from the container, the Tracking history will remain. New items can be added to the container.
        
    2.  Click the **Empty Container** button to remove all items from the container. 
        
        1.  The prompt to remove all items from the container will display.  
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/1a5dc72b-e9d6-46b9-863a-b1cbfda88c15)
            
        2.  When OK is clicked, another prompt to start a new Tracking Log for the container will display.
            
            1.  **Cancel** \- Click **Cancel** to retain the Tracking entries for historical reference.
                
            2.  **OK** \- Click **OK** to delete the Tracking entries.
                
9.  To print the contents of a container, select a configured Container Details report and click the Print button. See the [**Example: Container Details Report**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerDetailsReport "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerDetailsReport") section for more information. A PDF will generate similar to the following:  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/903ed0d5-6ce9-4595-b2db-e212531768c7)
    
10.  You may attempt to add an item that’s already in Container A to Container B. At this time, remove the item from Container A first before adding it to Container B.
    

## Add Items to Container - Hand Scanner

### (Video 1:25)

This video demonstrates how to work with containers using a hand scanner.

<iframe allowfullscreen="" allowtransparency="true" data-hasbody="false" data-layout="default" data-local-id="e5cd346f-cb10-4e52-bfcf-ddea3fbdd220" data-macro-id="ef85ecc7-6d50-4644-8136-b2ec54cd20c6" data-macro-name="widget" frameborder="0" height="364" mozallowfullscreen="" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="640" src="https://player.vimeo.com/video/347084881?h=embed"></iframe>

**To select and add items to a container using a hand scanner:**

1.  To select a container with a Hand Scanner, go to the Containers page.
    
2.  Click the **Scan Container QR code using handheld scanner** button.
    
3.  The button will disable indicating the container's QR code is ready for you to scan.
    
4.  Before you scan, make sure the page is active or has focus. You’ll know the Containers page is not active if you scan a container’s QR code and nothing happens. If this happens, just click anywhere on the containers page to give the page focus. 
    
5.  Go ahead and scan the container QR code. Notice that the Scan Success message will display. It will disappear in 2 seconds and you can scan the next item.
    
6.  The Container and any existing contents will display.
    
7.  Once a container is selected, you can add a package, assembly, or part to the container.
    
    1.  **Add Assembly on Scan checkbox**
        
        1.  **Checked** \- If checked, when a tracking status change is made to any part contained in an assembly, the change will automatically apply to all parts in the assembly and to the assembly itself.
            
        2.  **Unchecked** \- If unchecked, when a tracking status change is made to any part contained in an assembly, the change will not be applied to the any other parts or to the assembly.
            
8.  Click the **Scan item QR codes to add to container using Handheld scanner** button and then scan the QR code.
    
9.  The scanned item will display in the Contents list. Note that the Assembly or Package name is a hyperlink. The Assembly's link goes to the Assemblies Viewer and the Package's link goes to the tab you have set as the default for packages.
    
10.  If you scan an item that has already been scanned, the item will not be added to the container's contents list and you will be prompted to remove the item from the other container.
    

### Scan Errors

Scanned code was not in the expected format

If the message below displays when scanning a QR code on the Containers > Assign tab, it means that scanned content is case sensitive. To fix the issue, find a scanner setting that does not edit the text (Ex. changing text to all caps).

## Add Items to Container - Tablet or Phone Camera Scanner

**To select and add items to a container using a tablet or phone camera scanner:**

1.  Click the **Scan Container QR code using camera** button.
    
2.  When prompted to access the camera, click **Allow**.
    
3.  The **Scan Container QR Code with Camera or Reader** popup dialog will display.
    
    1.  If your device has 2 cameras, you can switch between the cameras.
        
    2.  The camera is ready to scan the QR code.
        
    3.  Position the device’s camera so that the QR code can be read.
        
4.  The device will scan the container label as soon as it can read the QR code. There’s no need to click any button to scan the QR code.
    
      
    As soon as the QR code is read, a Scan Successful popup message will display. This message will display for 2 seconds giving you time to move the scanner away from the current QR code.
    
5.  The Container and any existing contents will display.
    
6.  Once a container is selected, you can add a package, assembly, or part to the container.
    
7.  Click the **Scan item QR codes to add to container using Camera** button and then scan the QR code.
    
    1.  The correct camera should still be active.
        
8.  Position the device’s camera until the QR code is read.
    
9.  The **Scan Successful** popup message will display, and the scanned item will display in the Contents list.
    
10.  This message will display for 2 seconds giving you time to move the scanner away from the current QR code.
    
11.  The camera is ready to scan the next QR code.
    
12.  If you scan an item that has already been scanned, the item will not be added to the container's contents list and you will be prompted to remove the item from the other container.
    

## Move Items to a Different Container

## Move Items to a Different Container - Manual

To manually move items (part, assembly, package, or container) from one container to another:

1.  The Pallet 01 container currently includes SPOOL-02.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/12b40f67-73aa-4e29-92e4-b62b47905963)
    
2.  In the Manual Selection section, select the Project, Model, and then, in this case, the Assembly.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/339b4c46-568b-4745-8b8c-a94ecad3ab86)
    
3.  Click the **Add Assembly to Container** button. A "Move items" dialog similar to the following will display.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/2f43a170-4dbe-4145-b8f6-a6dcb90fd3ea)
    
4.  Click Move to move the item to the target container. The item will be moved and will display in the container.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/2d331b98-cf20-4d41-9a99-527cef28e3c1)
    
5.  The item will be removed from the original container.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/80fb71bf-812e-49bc-83da-3841dee6639b)
    

## Move Items to a Different Container - Scan

To move items (part, assembly, package, or container) from one container to another by using a scanner:

1.  The Pallet 01 container currently includes Spool 106.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/b42d80a4-e800-4757-aec0-41e68fbb37f5)
    
2.  To move Spool 106 to Pallet 02, make Pallet 02 active under Containers and click the **Scan item QR codes to add to container using handheld scanner** button or the **Scan item QR codes to add to container using camer** button.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/f0885db5-13ad-4fc8-9260-bcb7806c8c05)
    
3.  Scan the Spool 106 QR Code. The item will be moved to the target container and there will not be a prompt.
    
4.  Spool 106 is moved to Pallet 02.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/4915a901-0919-4395-828b-d4ccbb82db49)
    
5.  Spool 106 is removed from Pallet 01.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/bbdf14d9-f86a-42d3-abd8-54d7fe9ae225)
    

## Container Tracking Log Entry

A Container Tracking log entry is made whenever a package, assembly, part, or container is added to or removed from a container and when a container or container contents are moved to another container. This feature provides customers with either a permanent container tracking history or a history that is temporary and can be cleared. **Note**: The contents of a nested container will not be updated.

Container events (add, remove, empty) are logged in the applicable container, package, assembly, and part’s tracking log, so the history of what happened related to a container is transparent. The Contents column displays the contents of the container at the time of the event. Updates will be visible in the following locations:

1.  **Container Tracking**
    
2.  **Package Tracking**
    
3.  **Assembly Tracking**
    
4.  **Part Property**
    
5.  **QR Code Scanned page (Assembly example)**
    

## Add Container A to Container B (Sub-container)

If a container is included within another container, the sub-container can be managed (Empty Container and Remove Item) as if it were the selected container so that the user does not have to switch between containers.

In the example below, items were added to the Hanger Box container and then the Hanger Box container was added to the Truck D container.

1.  **Parent Container section**
    
    1.  **Parent Container** - The parent container is the container selected in the Container drop-down.
        
    2.  **Empty Container** button - Click the **Empty Container** button associated with Truck D to empty the container of all items.
        
    3.  **Remove** item button - Click the **Remove** button to remove individual items from the parent container.
        
2.  **Containers sub-section**
    
    1.  **Sub-container** - A sub-container displays after a container is added to the parent container.
        
    2.  **Remove sub-container Hanger Box** button - Click the **Remove sub-container Hanger Box** button to remove the Hanger Box sub-container from the Truck D parent container. The container will be removed from Truck D.
        
    3.  **Empty Container** button - Click the **Empty Container** button associated with sub-container to empty the sub-container of all items. **Note**: All items will also be removed from the sub-container when it is selected as the parent container.
        
    4.  **Remove** item button - Click the **Remove** button to remove individual items from the sub-container.
        

## Reports

## Container

A Container report includes information about the container, not the contents of the container. Before a Container label can be printed, it must be configured.

-   See the [**Example: Container Label Report**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerLabelReport "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerLabelReport") section for more information.
    
-   To Print Container Label, see the [**Print Container Label**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/246317057/Containers+Admin#Print-Container-Label "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/246317057/Containers+Admin#Print-Container-Label") section.
    
-   To see a list of [**STRATUS.Container.\***](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/598868043/STRATUS.+Parameters+and+Properties#STRATUS.Container.* "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/598868043/STRATUS.+Parameters+and+Properties#STRATUS.Container.*") fields that can be used as Container fields on report.
    

A Container Label can be printed from:

1.  The Containers (Admin) page or from the [**Containers**](http://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers "http://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers") page by clicking the Print Labels button.
    
2.  The Containers page by clicking the Print Labels button.
    

## Container Details

A Container Details report includes the contents of a container, not information about the container. A Container Details report is run from the Container’s page. Before a Container report can be generated, it must be configured. See the [**Example: Container Details Report**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerDetailsReport "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerDetailsReport") section for more information.  

![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/1c2bccf9-85e6-4e21-b81b-ddd355e6c9f2)

## Container Part, Assembly, or Package Report

A Container Part, Assembly, or Package report is targeted to Shop or Field workers to provide them with container information to help locate items. See the [**Example: Container Part, Assembly, or Package Report**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerPart%2CAssembly%2CorPackageReport "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerPart%2CAssembly%2CorPackageReport") section for more information.

## Print Container Label

A Container Label can be printed from the Containers (Admin) page or from the [**Containers**](http://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers "http://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/188514329/Containers") page once a container has been selected. Before a Container label can be printed, it must be configured. See the [**Example: Container Label Report**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerLabelReport "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10617393/Reports+Admin#Example%3AContainerLabelReport") section for more information.

1.  Open the **GTP Stratus Print** and check that it is pointing to the correct company, tool, and label printer. Download the [**GTP Stratus Print**](https://www.dropbox.com/sh/4hftsujfunksicx/AAAlklSQs3ZUbMin3yaMC0-Ia?dl=0 "https://www.dropbox.com/sh/4hftsujfunksicx/AAAlklSQs3ZUbMin3yaMC0-Ia?dl=0") if it’s not already installed.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/3c31bc30-61e9-4238-97a2-1ba17924bf92)
    
2.  Print a Container Label from either location below:
    
    1.  Under **Admin** > **Company** > **Containers** click the **Print Labels** button for any container.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/cfbc59a6-0b09-4447-b40a-d74b210b8753)
        
    2.  Under Containers > Print Label button.
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/ff2dbe14-1c4d-4979-a647-83f7881050fd)
        
3.  You will be prompted to **Select Printer Tool**.
    
    1.  **Select the tool that will be used to print the labels** – This is the Printer Tool configured above.
        
    2.  **Select the ZPL Container Report with the desired Label Template** – This is the Container Label Report configured above.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/0e03bbca-3003-40c6-8913-b7c013d41a39)
        
4.  Click **OK** and the label will print. Below is an example of a Container Label.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/9781554c-74f8-4eb2-98c8-0b871ba9ec4f)
    

## Scan and Report Mode

Scan and Report Mode is a feature that streamlines the process of adding items to multiple containers and then generating a report with minimal interaction on the Containers Assign page.

To setup this feature:

1.  Select the Report that should be generated when the process of adding items to the container is complete. In this example, the Container Details report is selected which is the Bill of Lading.
    
2.  Open the first container.
    
3.  Click the **Scan and Report Mode** button. It will turn from green to blue to indicate it is active. With the feature ready to use scan items into the container.
    
4.  Scan items into the container. In this example, 1 assembly and 4 loose parts are added to the container.
    
5.  When done with this container, scan the next container QR code.
    
6.  As the next container populates the Assign tab, the selected report will automatically generate in a separate window for the existing container. The report might need to be manually printed.
    
7.  Continue to scan items into the newly selected container. 4 assemblies will be scanned into this container and each includes a tracking log entry.
    
8.  When done, scan the next container QR code.
    
9.  The report will generate.
    
10.  Repeat this process of scanning and generating a container report as needed. To end the Scan and Report Mode, click the **Scan and Report Mode** button. It will turn back to green.
    

## Scan the Container QR Code

Scan the Container QR Code to review the container's contents and update the Tracking Status.

To scan a container's QR Code:

1.  Print a Container Label.
    
2.  Scan the QR Code to display the **Container QR Code Scanned** landing page where the Contents of the Container can be expanded, emptied, and the status of the container can be updated which changes the status of the packages, assemblies, and parts within the container.
    
3.  To Add Images or Attachments to a Tracking Status update:
    
    1.  Click the **Capture Image** or the **Add Attachments** button to add an image or attachment to the tracking status update.

# Containers Dashboard - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Container Dashboard provides information about each container and its contents.  See the Containers (Admin) article for more information on how to configure containers.

---
The Container Dashboard provides information about each container and its contents.  See the **[Containers (Admin)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/246317057/Containers+Admin)** article for more information on how to configure containers.

-   1[Summary](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877573633/Containers+Dashboard#ContainersDashboard-Summary)
-   2[Container Report Properties](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877573633/Containers+Dashboard#ContainersDashboard-ContainerReportProperties)

## Summary

1.  By default, the Dashboard displays a Default report for the Report. **Note**: When a container is expanded the selected Details Report will displays (see below).
    
2.  **Report Table (Default) - Collapsed Container![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/attachments/1877573633/image2023-1-17_15-10-52.png?version=1&modificationDate=1673989853873&cacheVersion=1&api=v2)**
    
    1.  **Expand / Collapse** - Expand the container to display the Details Report showing the container contents, or, collapse the container details. The expander will only display if the container includes at least one item.
        
    2.  **Type - The type of container defined under Admin > Company > Containers.**
        
    3.  **Name** \- The name of the container defined under Admin > Company > Containers.
        
    4.  **State**
        
        1.  **In Use** - Indicates that at least one item is in the container.
            
        2.  **Empty** \- Indicates that the container is empty.
            
    5.  **Description** \- The description of the container defined under Admin > Company > Containers.
        
    6.  **Length** \- The length of the container defined under Admin > Company > Containers.
        
    7.  **Height** \- The height of the container defined under Admin > Company > Containers.
        
    8.  **Width** \- The width of the container defined under Admin > Company > Containers.
        
    9.  **Required** \- If there is a package in the container, the required date is derived from the most recent Field date located under Packages > Properties > Planning > Field.
        
    10.  **Status** \- The status of the container set on the under Containers > Assign.
        
    11.  **Division** - Once a container status has been set, a Division can be assigned.
    12.  **Attachments** \- Displays a link to any attachments made to the container under Containers > Assign.
        
3.  **Details Report Table (Default) - Expanded Container**
    
    ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/1877573633/image2022-5-9_9-56-57.png?version=1&modificationDate=1652108218829&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=1100&height=586)
    
    1.  **#** - A sequence number for the items in the container.
        
    2.  **Type - The type of item (package, assembly, or part)**
        
    3.  **Name** \- The name of the item (package name, assembly name, or part name).
        
    4.  **Project** \- The project from which the item was included.
        
    5.  **Model** \- The model from which the item was included. Also includes a link to the model.
        
    6.  **Package** \- The package from which the item was included. Also includes a link to the package.
        
    7.  **QR Code** - Opens the QR Scanned page.
        
    8.  **Attachments** \- Displays a link to any attachments made to the container under Containers > Assign.
        
4.  **Custom Reports** - Custom reports will populate the Report and Details Report drop-downs as follows:
    
    1.  **Report**
        
        1.  Item Type = Container
            
        2.  Container Dashboard = Checked
            
    2.  **Details Report**
        
        1.  Item Type = Container Details
            
        2.  Container Dashboard = Checked
            

## Container Report Properties

See the [**STRATUS.Container.\***](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/598868043/STRATUS.+Parameters+and+Properties#STRATUS.*ParametersandProperties-STRATUS.Container.*) section for more information on Container fields.

# Create Package - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> Stratus recognizes parts, assemblies, and packages.  After publishing the Revit model or AutoCAD drawing to Stratus, parts and assemblies (if created in Revit or AutoCAD) are available in Stratus. Assemblies can also be created in Stratus. A package can include parts and assemblies. Stratus supports the workflow whereby different packages can be created for different purposes like ordering, shop work, field delivery, and installation work. Package Categories accommodate workflows where the same part or assembly needs to be included in multiple package categories.  A package must be in the "Can Package" tracking status in order to add/remove elements.

---
Stratus recognizes parts, assemblies, and packages.  After publishing the Revit model or AutoCAD drawing to Stratus, parts and assemblies (if created in Revit or AutoCAD) are available in Stratus. Assemblies can also be created in Stratus. A package can include parts and assemblies. Stratus supports the workflow whereby different packages can be created for different purposes like ordering, shop work, field delivery, and installation work. [Package Categories](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351") accommodate workflows where the same part or assembly needs to be included in multiple package categories.  A package must be in the ["Can Package" tracking status](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761") in order to add/remove elements.

-   1 [Create New Package](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/67502081/Create+Package#Create-New-Package)
-   2 [Add Parts and Assemblies to a Package - Model Viewer](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/67502081/Create+Package#Add-Parts-and-Assemblies-to-a-Package---Model-Viewer)
-   3 [Locked Package](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/67502081/Create+Package#Locked-Package)
-   4 [Videos](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/67502081/Create+Package#Videos)

## Create New Package

A built-in package Lead Days feature was added to Stratus on 8/7/2021 that offers calculated default Start Dates for package phases. With this change, those who create Packages must set the **Required Date** in relation to a Package **Phase**. Phases are also used in [**Division (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103317524 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103317524") and [**Tracking Statuses (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761"). See the [**Added Lead Days and Start Date Properties to Packages**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1662813138#Added-Lead-Days-and-Start-Date-Properties-to-Packages "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1662813138#Added-Lead-Days-and-Start-Date-Properties-to-Packages") section for more information.

Below are the package Phases in relation to Lead Days:

-   **Office** \- Detailing Start Date
    
-   **Purchasing** \- Purchasing Start Date
    
-   **Shop** \- Fabrication Start Date
    
-   **Field** (Default) - Required On-site Date
    

**To create a package in the Models Viewer or Packages Viewer:**

1.  Before creating a package:
    
    1.  The **Package Name** and **Package Number** should be configured under [**Naming Conventions**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913").
        
    2.  One or more **Package Categories** should be configured under [**Package Categories**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351").
        
2.  Go to **Models** > **Viewer** > **Actions** > **Packages** > **New**. You can also create a new package under **Packages** > **Dashboard** > **New Package**. The new package dialog and package name fields, similar to the following, will display.
    
    1.  **Category (Required)** - Select the package Category. See the [**Package Categories (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351") article for more information.
        
    2.  **Number** and **Name** - The package **Number** and **Name** will be filled-in automatically if you have configured [**Naming Conventions**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913"). You can overwrite any field value, however, each package name must be unique.
        
    3.  **Description (Optional)** \- Enter a Description as needed.
        
    4.  **Hours Estimated (Optional)** \- Enter Hours Estimated as needed.
        
    5.  **Phase (Required)** - Select a package Phase.
        
        1.  **Field (Default)** - Field is selected by default which is equivalent to how packages have has always been created. The Field Phase Required Date is the Start Date that the package materials are required to be on-site and ready for fieldwork to begin.
            
        2.  **Office, Purchasing, Shop** - Select the Phase for packages that need a Start Date for Office, Purchasing, or Shop work to begin. If Lead Days have been configured for the Phase and Category, then Phase Start Dates, including the Field Required Date will be calculated. If Lead Days have not been configured, then all Phases will have the same Start Date.
            
    6.  **Required Date** - Enter a **Required Date** for the selected Phase. The Required Date may or may not be calculated depending on which Phase is selected and which Lead Day settings have been configured.
        
        1.  **Field (Default)** - If Phase = Field, then the Required Date on the Packages Dashboard (Default Report) will be set to the Required Date. See the screenshot below.
            
        2.  **Office, Purchasing, Shop** - If Phase = Office, Purchasing, or Shop, then the Required Date on the Packages Dashboard (Default Report) will be calculated based on Lead Day settings.
            
            1.  **Lead Days configured** - If Lead Days have been configured for the Phase and selected Category, then the Required Date displayed on the Packages Dashboard will be calculated.
                
            2.  **Lead Days not configured** - If no Lead Days have been configured for the Phase and selected Category, then the Required Date displayed on the Packages Dashboard will be the Required Date and all Phases will have the same Start Date.
                
            3.  See the [**Added Lead Days and Start Date Properties to Packages**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1662813138#Added-Lead-Days-and-Start-Date-Properties-to-Packages "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1662813138#Added-Lead-Days-and-Start-Date-Properties-to-Packages") section for more information.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/ea1840d8-6d87-42e1-bbd6-b14cbad6d68e)
                
    7.  **BIM Area** - Stratus will attempt to assign a BIM Area to the Package. 
        
        1.  The BIM Area option list displays in the New Package dialog.
            
        2.  **Notes:**
            
            1.  The BIM Area assignment will **not** update the Stratus.Part.BIMArea property which is the BIM Area associated with the part.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/50282587-e5ae-4292-89a1-286d8fc476c3)
                
            2.  The BIM Area assignment will only update the Stratus.Package.BIMAreaPath property which can be included on a Packages Dashboard report (BIM Area below). **Note**: The Stratus.Package.BIMAreaPath is editable on the Packages Dashboard.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/09a4656e-6c70-4e47-9793-859e63739bf5)
                
        3.  **BIM Area Selection**
            
            1.  **All parts are in a single BIM Area** 
                
                1.  When all parts are located within a single BIM Area, the BIM Area is selected by default. The BIM Area can be changed to None or the BIM Area’s parent area.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/fb27980e-ffec-4155-8cba-7e7565572ecc)
                    
                2.  Once the package is created the selected BIM Area will display under Packages > Properties > General section.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/7949e7b9-a752-4a53-a738-74295370799a)
                    
                3.  The BIM Area can be edited here. Click the drop-down. If a new BIM Area is selected, click the **Save** button.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/e7163ea9-ca3c-4788-8469-63e175043b74)
                    
                4.  The package’s BIM Area assignment will display on any Packages Dashboard report that includes the Stratus.Package.BIMAreaPath property.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/c8164a17-49c3-4afb-a29b-1be7f0fbe67e)
                    
            2.  Parts are in Multiple BIM Areas
                
                1.  When parts are located in multiple BIM Areas, the BIM Area that contains the most selected parts (19) is selected by default. The BIM Area can be changed to a different BIM Area, None, or the BIM Area’s parent area.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/f97bfeaa-6e86-4396-ba0a-b751d11bd47f)
                    
                2.  Once the package is created the selected BIM Area will display under Packages > Properties > General section. The BIM Area can be edited here.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/2ea738a6-0176-4184-bac2-416345c255c2)
                    
                3.  The BIM Area can be edited here. Click the drop-down. If a new BIM Area is selected, click the **Save** button.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/9cb3b79e-614a-4146-8adb-2fd0a4bb32a1)
                    
                4.  The package’s BIM Area assignment will display on any Packages Dashboard report that includes the Stratus.Package.BIMAreaPath property.  
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/861d2d28-fcac-4c08-8d7e-c75c8cd65684)
                    
3.  Click **Save Package** when done. A package similar to the following will be saved. Parts and assemblies can now be added to or removed from the package.
    
4.  Information about packages displays on the **Packages** > **Dashboard**.
    
5.  New packages are automatically added to the **Packages** > **Schedule**. 
    

## Add Parts and Assemblies to a Package - Model Viewer

If parts were not selected while create a New Package, parts or assemblies can be added to the package. There are several ways to add parts or assemblies to a package.  Note: Before adding parts or assemblies to a package, the package must be in a "**Can Package**" tracking status. See the [**Tracking Statuses**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761") page for more information. For example, if a package is the "Shipped" tracking status, it's not a good practice to edit the package by adding a part or assembly to it.

To add parts and assemblies to a package:

1.  In the **Models** > **Viewer**, click **Actions** > **Packages** and select your target package.
    
2.  In the **Models** > **Viewer**, **Filter** the model as needed.
    
    1.  If everything isolated in view will be added to the package, click the **\+ Isolated Assemblies/Parts** button. The isolated elements will be added to the package. 
        
    2.  If, you selected parts and assemblies, click the + Selected **Assemblies/Parts** button. The selected elements will be added to the package. 
        
3.  Once added to a package, parts, and assemblies will display on the Package's **Items** tab. 
    
4.  There is an art to isolating and selecting items in the Models Viewer. For information on different ways to add/remove elements to/from a package, see the Create Package video on this page. Some techniques like the Select Connected tool and Auto-Assembly tool rely on a good model where all parts are connected. 
    

## Locked Package

A Package becomes "Locked" when the Package is in a Tracking Status that does not have "Can Package" checked under Admin > Company > Tracking Statuses.

## **Videos**

**Create Package (4:34) -** This video, created on 4/3/2018, does not include some new features (naming conventions and package category) but does demonstrate how to add elements to and remove elements from a package:

1.  How to select or create a new package.
    
2.  How to see all packages on the Packages Dashboard.
    
3.  How to add elements (parts and spools) to a package by filtering the model or manually selecting elements.
    
4.  How to delete a package.
    
5.  How to remove elements from a package.

# Create and Manage Assemblies - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> Adding model elements to an assembly is straightforward. Select an existing or new assembly, select elements from the model, and then add the elements to the assembly. Once added to an assembly, they will display on the Assemblies page.  Parts can only be added to one assembly but can be added to multiple packages.  Stratus will give a warning/question if the part already resides in a different assembly.

---
Adding model elements to an assembly is straightforward. Select an existing or new assembly, select elements from the model, and then add the elements to the assembly. Once added to an assembly, they will display on the Assemblies page.  Parts can only be added to one assembly but can be added to multiple packages.  Stratus will give a warning/question if the part already resides in a different assembly.

-   1 [Assembly Management](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Assembly-Management)
    -   1.1 [Create Assembly](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Create-Assembly)
    -   1.2 [Delete Assembly](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Delete-Assembly)
    -   1.3 [Add / Remove Assembly Parts](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Add-%2F-Remove-Assembly-Parts)
-   2 [Tracking Status for Newly Created Assembly](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Tracking-Status-for-Newly-Created-Assembly)
-   3 [Auto Assemblies Video](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Auto-Assemblies-Video)
-   4 [Auto Assemblies](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Auto-Assemblies)
-   5 [Clear Assembly Button](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Clear-Assembly-Button)
-   6 [Create Assembly in Revit](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Create-Assembly-in-Revit)
-   7 [Remove Item From Assembly when the Assembly is part of a Package](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Remove-Item-From-Assembly-when-the-Assembly-is-part-of-a-Package)
-   8 [Move a Single Part to a Different Assembly](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Move-a-Single-Part-to-a-Different-Assembly)
-   9 [Can Package Unchecked](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Can-Package-Unchecked)
-   10 [Unique Assembly Instances in Revit](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315/Create+and+Manage+Assemblies#Unique-Assembly-Instances-in-Revit)

## Assembly Management

### Create Assembly

A Stratus assembly can be created:

-   During the model publish process when an assembly had been created in the model and where within Stratus under Admin > Company > Settings > the Assembly Conflict Resolution for Revit or AutoCAD is set to AutoCAD is always right, Revit is always right, or Prompt User and AutoCAD or Revit is selected. See the [**Settings (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10518994 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10518994") for more information.
    
-   **Under Models > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies**
    
-   **Under Packages > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies**
    

In the latter 2 cases, the Actions > Assemblies feature displays and functions the same and there is a manual and [**Auto Assemblies**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/pages/resumedraft.action?draftId=65634315#CreateandManageAssemblies-AutoAssemblies "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/pages/resumedraft.action?draftId=65634315#CreateandManageAssemblies-AutoAssemblies") option. Most companies create assemblies after creating packages. 

**Note:** Before an assembly is created, deleted, or edited check that the assembly, package or the targeted parts in the model are in a **Can Assemble Tracking Status**. See the [**Tracking Statuses (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761") article for more information.

**To create a new assembly using the Actions > Assemblies feature:**

1.  In the Models or Packages Viewer select Actions > Assemblies. The Assemblies dialog will display.
    
2.  Optionally, under Filters > Assemblies, click the **Unassigned Parts** checkbox to help identify which parts are not yet in an assembly. The parts in the viewer will be filtered. 
    
3.  Select the parts to be added to the new assembly and then click **New**, or vice versa. The Assembly naming fields configured under Admin > Company > Naming and Numbering > Naming Conventions > Assembly Naming will display and populate based on the parts selected. See the [**Naming and Numbering (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/164134913") article for more information.
    
    1.  **Name** - To override any of the naming fields, click the Name checkbox. 
        
4.  When done, click **Save Assembly** button. The following displays:
    
    1.  The Assembly is created and its name displays in the Actions panel and in the Filters panel.
        
    2.  In the Actions panel, the assembly name is also a link to open the assembly in the Assemblies Viewer. See the [**Assemblies Viewer**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081") article for more information.
        
    3.  If the Unassigned Parts checkbox is checked, the parts will have disappeared from the viewer.
        
    4.  The assembly displays on the Assemblies Dashboard.
        
    5.  **Note** : When creating an EMPTY assembly in the Packages Viewer, the assembly takes on the status of the Package/Parts being added. 
        

### Delete Assembly

A Stratus assembly can be deleted:

-   During the model publish process where an assembly has been deleted in the model and where within Stratus under Admin > Company > Settings > the Assembly Conflict Resolution for Revit or AutoCAD is set to AutoCAD is always right, Revit is always right, or Prompt User and AutoCAD or Revit is selected. See the [**Settings (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10518994 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10518994") for more information.
    
-   **Under Assemblies > Dashboard** - See the [**Assemblies Dashboard**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8912924 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8912924") article for more information.
    
-   **Under Packages > Items** - See the [**Package Items**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166658049 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166658049") article for more information.
    

**Note:** Before an assembly is created, deleted, or edited check that the assembly, package or the targeted parts in the model are in a **Can Assemble Tracking Status**. See the [**Tracking Statuses (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10485761") article for more information.

### Add / Remove Assembly Parts

Assembly parts can be added and removed:

-   During the model publish process when an assembly had been edited in the model and where within Stratus under Admin > Company > Settings > the Assembly Conflict Resolution for Revit or AutoCAD is set to AutoCAD is always right, Revit is always right, or Prompt User and AutoCAD or Revit is selected. See the [**Settings (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10518994 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/10518994") for more information.
    
-   **Under Packages > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies**
    
-   **Under Models > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies**
    

In the latter 2 cases, the Actions > Assemblies feature displays and functions the same. 

**Packages > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies - Add / Remove parts for an existing assembly** 

1.  Open the package that contains the assembly in the Packages > Viewer.
    
2.  Locate the assembly.
    
    1.  Optionally, open the Filters > Assemblies and check the target assembly checkbox.
        
    2.  Optionally, open the Filters > Assemblies and check the Unassigned Parts checkbox.
        
3.  Select one or more parts to add/remove. In this example, a part to add has been selected. The Add Selected and Remove Selected buttons become enabled.
    
    1.  **Add** - Click the **Add Selected** button. The parts will be added to the assembly.
        
    2.  **Remove** - Click the **Remove Selected** button. The parts will be removed from the assembly.
        

**Models > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies - Add / Remove parts for an existing assembly** 

**Tips**:

-   Once an assembly is selected in the viewer, press the F key to zoom/focus onto the assembly.
    
-   To select a part that is included in an assembly, hover over the part, press tab, and then click the left mouse to select the individual part.
    

1.  Open the **Models > Viewer > Actions > Assemblies** and use one of the following methods to select the assembly. 
    
    1.  Select the assembly in the drop-down under **Actions > Assemblies.**
        
    2.  Select the assembly in the **Models > Viewer.**
        
    3.  Open **Filters > Assemblies,** check the assembly, and then select the assembly in the **Models > Viewer**.
        
2.  To add one or more parts to the assembly, select the part(s) (not in the assembly) to be added to the assembly.
    
    1.  Click the **Add Selected** button. The parts will be added to the assembly.
        
3.  To remove one or more parts from the assembly, select the part(s) (in the assembly).
    
    1.  Click the **Remove Selected** button. The parts will be removed from the assembly.
        

## Tracking Status for Newly Created Assembly

A newly created assembly will be assigned the first tracking status where the **Applies to Assembly** checkbox is checked. The parts in the assembly will be assigned the first tracking status in the list because parts can belong to multiple packages in different categories and customers have stated that they don't want the part status to immediately change.

In this example:

1.  Under Admin > Company > Tracking Statuses, the first tracking status whose **Applies to Assembly** checkbox is checked is **Issued**.
    
2.  As a result, when a new assembly is created:
    
    1.  The **assembly tracking status** will be Issued.
        
    2.  The **tracking status of parts in the assembly** will be Design, the first tracking status in the list.
        

## Auto Assemblies Video

<iframe allowfullscreen="" allowtransparency="true" data-hasbody="false" data-layout="default" data-local-id="e9488b09-92b6-41ca-be52-557566029190" data-macro-id="2c33d29b2d96e839f46aae352e45a74cc33d8e6d56956c1a91e453b107a2d029" data-macro-name="widget" frameborder="0" height="364" mozallowfullscreen="" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="640" src="https://player.vimeo.com/video/1076513946?h=29d26bae08"></iframe>

## Auto Assemblies

1.  The Auto Assemblies or Continuous Spooling feature is included in the Model Viewer and Package Viewer under **Actions** > **Assemblies**. This feature enables users to start spooling by selecting one part and then through a series of clicks, tell Stratus when the spool ends and where the next one begins.
    
2.  To use the Auto Assemblies feature, check the following:
    
    1.  Be sure the system you want to auto assemble is connected. Click the **Selected Connected** tool and then click a part in the system. If the connected system turns to blue (selected) then Auto Assemblies will work. If not, discuss the connection issue with the modeler. 
        
    2.  Make sure that **Assembly Selection** and **Multiple Part Selection** options are unchecked.
        
    3.  Make sure that no parts are selected.
        
    4.  When clicking parts avoid selecting couplings and welds as Stratus ignores these parts.
        
3.  To keep track of which parts have been added to an assembly, it is recommended that Display Modes for Assemblies be selected. The Display Modes button remains green after the panel is closed indicating that it is active and parts added to assemblies will change color.
    
4.  To use the Auto Assemblies tool in the Models Viewer or Package Viewer, go to **Actions** > **Assemblies** and click the **Auto Assemblies** button. 
    
5.  The dialog switches to **Set Start** and **Finish**. In addition, the assembly naming convention configured by the administrator will display.
    
    1.  **Set Start** - The purpose of the **Set Start** button is to clear the spool start number and allows you to start spooling with a clean slate. You don’t have to use this button, but is can be useful when you start spooling a separate system or a branch.
        
    2.  **Finish** - The purpose of the **Finish** button is to close out the continuous spool command. While the continuous spool command is active it watches the clicks and generates the assemblies.
        
6.  To start the process, click the **Set Start** button. Go ahead and zoom in to select the starting part that will be included in the first assembly. Once selected, notice the following in the assembly naming section:
    
    1.  The message loading **BIM Areas** displays indicating that a part was selected.
        
    2.  The naming convention fields can be populated.
        
    3.  A **Spool Start** number is displayed.
        
7.  **Click the end part** of the first assembly. As the assembly is being created, the red bar displays.
    
8.  Once the assembly is created:
    
    1.  The red bar disappears.
        
    2.  The parts in between the first and last part selected will change color if Display Modes > Assemblies is active.
        
    3.  The **Spool Start** number changes to a new number indicating that the next connected part is set to be the first part in the next assembly.
        
9.  Since the first part in the next assembly is automatically selected, to create the next assembly, only the end part of the second assembly needs to be clicked. Like before, wait for the red bar to go away, the Spool Start number to change, and the in between parts to change color.
    
10.  Continue clicking the next end part and wait for the color to change. You can zoom and pan during this process without impacting the Auto Assemblies workflow.
    
11.  With the last part in this connected run added to an assembly, **Spool Start** is now blank and with no part selected the naming convention returns to default.
    
12.  If done auto assembling, click the **Finish** button. If there are other branches that need to be assembled, repeat the process from step 6 if the **Set Start** and **Finish** buttons are still in the Assemblies panel, otherwise, start from the beginning.
    
13.  Created assemblies display in all the usual places including under Display Modes > Assemblies, Filters > Assemblies, Assemblies Dashboard, and Packages > Dashboard > Items to name a few.
    

## Clear Assembly Button

1.  Under **Models** > **Actions** > **Assemblies**, a button has been added to clear the assembly selector which will make it easier to select a spool and edit it.
    
2.  For example, when you select an assembly under Models > Actions > Assemblies, Stratus thinks you want to add or remove parts from the assembly. But, let’s say you just want to clear the selected assembly.
    
3.  Now you can click the button next to the currently selected assembly.
    
4.  The Assemblies panel will clear and be set to NONE.
    

## Create Assembly in Revit

The GTP Stratus Add-in for Revit, in addition to the Publish and Import commands, also provides a **Create Assembly** option that gives you the ability to spool in Revit using the Stratus naming conventions defined by your company administrator. This is a good option for those who prefer to spool inside Revit.

**To use the Create Assembly option:**

1.  Open a model in Revit.
    
2.  Select items to be included in a spool or assembly.
    
3.  Under Add-Ins > GTP Stratus, click the **Create Assembly** button. The Stratus Create Assembly dialog will display.
    
4.  Hover over a field to see which information should be entered. When assemblies are created within Stratus, these fields are populated automatically.
    
5.  When done, click save and the assembly will be created. 
    
6.  Once the model is published, the assembly will be visible in Stratus.
    

## Remove Item From Assembly when the Assembly is part of a Package

-   If you have created a package
    
-   And, the package includes an assembly of parts
    
-   And then, you remove one or more parts from an assembly
    
-   The part will be listed as separate part in the package. Here’s an example where the 2 parts were removed from one of the above assemblies.
    

## Move a Single Part to a Different Assembly

To move a single part from one assembly to another assembly:

1.  The target assembly and the assembly that contains the part being moved must be in a **tracking status** where **Can Assemble** **is checked**.
    
2.  Under **Actions** > **Assemblies**, select the target assembly.
    
3.  In the model, **hover** over the part that you want to move to a different assembly, press the **Tab** key, and the **click** the part. This should select the part, not the entire assembly.
    
4.  Click the **Add Selected Parts to Assembly** button.
    
5.  Click **OK** at the “**Move Parts From One Assembly To Another?”** prompt.
    
6.  The assembly and parts will be moved.
    

## Can Package Unchecked

When parts have been added to a package, and the package's tracking status is set to one where Can Package unchecked (Ex. Issued below), it also means that parts within the package cannot be added to an Assembly. This is true even if the tracking status has Can Assemble checked. Can Package being unchecked means that no changes can be made to the package.

## Unique Assembly Instances in Revit

A Shared Family parameter can be added to a parts family will force unique instances of assemblies in Revit. This is the same way Victaulic overcomes Revit’s feature that automatically creates multiple instances of a named assembly type. By including this shared parameter in Revit for pipe fittings, couplings, and welds for example, you can force separate assemblies when using Stratusfor Revit. 

**To use this feature:**

1.  Open a model.
    
2.  Create Shared Parameter under **Manage** > **Shared Parameters** > **New**
    
    1.  **Name**: Schedule Assembly Name
        
    2.  **Discipline**: Common
        
    3.  **Type of Parameter**: Text
        
3.  Double click and open a part.
    
4.  Click **Modify > Family Types > New Parameter > Shared Parameter > select the Schedule Assembly Name created above.**  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/6fdd7389-deb4-4989-84ff-46b1c9fed3f8)
    
    1.  Select **Instance parameter**.
        
5.  **Save** the family file.
    
6.  Go back to main model.
    
7.  **Insert** > **Load Family** > Family file just created.
    
8.  Next time a model is published using this shared parameter it will include unique instances of assemblies.

# Dashboard - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Projects Dashboard provides basic project information and the ability to change the project Status from New, to Active, to Archive. Only Active projects are visible to most users.

---
The Projects Dashboard provides basic project information and the ability to change the project Status from New, to Active, to Archive. Only Active projects are visible to most users.![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/3408239/image2025-1-29_12-37-46.png?version=1&modificationDate=1738175868346&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=1000&height=322)

Project information editing is done under Admin > Company > Projects where you can set the project Status, enter the project Number (which can be used in your company's naming convention, Description, City, State, Zip, Target Start Date, Target End Date, Tax Exempt, and Color which is used in dashboards.

![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/3408239/image2019-1-11_15-26-53.png?version=1&modificationDate=1547242015032&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=829&height=323)

# Deliverables - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> A Project Deliverable combines a model, filter, grouping (optional), and BIM area that enables automatic package deliverable creation. A deliverable is not a package, but, with a couple of clicks can be used to generate many packages at once without having to use the Models Viewer to manually filter and select each package. Deliverables can save your company time if you have well-defined project Areas, Filters, and Package Categories.

---
A Project Deliverable combines a model, filter, grouping (optional), and BIM area that enables automatic package deliverable creation. A deliverable is not a package, but, with a couple of clicks can be used to generate many packages at once without having to use the Models Viewer to manually filter and select each package. Deliverables can save your company time if you have well-defined project Areas, Filters, and Package Categories.
