## Stratus Academy Course Video

To take the Deliverables for Administrators course, login to [**Stratus Academy**](https://academy.stratus.build/ "https://academy.stratus.build/") and locate the course **ADM-517: Deliverables**.

To take the Deliverables for Managers course, login to [**Stratus Academy**](https://academy.stratus.build/ "https://academy.stratus.build/") and locate the course **MGR-310: Deliverables**.

## Deliverable Settings

## Company Deliverable Definitions

The first step in creating a project deliverable is to create company level **Deliverable Definition** which can be applied to any project under Admin > Company > Deliverable Definition. See the [**Deliverables Definitions (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/255393797 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/255393797") article for more information.

## Project Areas

Project deliverables are dependent on configured project Project Areas (Package Per Area Breakdown). The Package "Per Area Breakdown" number depends on the number of hierarchical areas defined in the project. For example, an AutoCAD model by default might only have the building as an area, whereas a Revit model might include a more granular hierarchical breakdown by Level, Scope Box, Room, etc. See the [**Areas (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742") article for more information.

The Deliverables page uses the Sort set on the Areas page. 

**To sort Deliverables:**

1.  Open the Projects > Areas page. On this page, the project model is imported, area abbreviations set, Range settings adjusted, and more. See the [**Areas (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742") article for more information.
    
2.  The Areas data can be sorted by Name or Elevation.
    
    1.  Click the **Sort by Name** button.
        
    2.  Or, click the **Sort by Elevation** button.
        
3.  Once the sort order is set, refresh the Projects > Deliverables page. The sort order will be the same as the Areas page.
    
    1.  Sort by Name (left) vs.  Sort by Elevation (right):
        

## Company Package Categories

A Package Category enables company's to create different packages for different purposes like Office, Purchasing, Shop, and Field work. See the [**Package Categories (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351") article for more information.

## Project Deliverables Settings

Project Deliverables leverage the Company [**Deliverable Definition**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/213123080 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/213123080") (**Deliverable and Grouping**), the Company [**Package Categories**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/166199351") (**Package Category**), the [**Project Areas**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742") (**Package Per Area Breakdown**), and limit the Deliverable to a specific model (**Models**). Once a company Deliverable Definition, Package Category, and Project Areas have been defined, then a **Project Deliverable** can be defined. A Project Deliverable breaks out all parts defined by the company Deliverable Definition which includes a part filter, Project Areas, and then applies a Package Category to those parts. In addition, the Deliverable is limited to a specific model. Package are not created at this time but are ready to be generated under the Projects > Deliverables tab as needed.

**To create a Project Deliverable:**

1.  On the Projects > Deliverables page, click the **Project Deliverables Settings** gear icon 
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/864dbe11-65d7-4e88-8ee7-aaa793e06fa9)
    
    .  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/1266e3d9-b6a1-47df-a046-be1fd87c5912)
    
2.  A **Project Deliverables Settings** dialog similar to the following will display.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/14cdcf14-a564-402f-a62d-728eef7c48a2)
    
3.  Click **New Deliverable**.
    
    1.  **Deliverable** – Select the company level Deliverable Definition previously defined under Admin > Company > Deliverables which includes the part filter.
        
    2.  **Package Category** – Select the package category that parts and assemblies will be assigned to once the deliverable is used to generate a package.
        
    3.  **Package Per Area Breakdown** – Select the smallest sub-area for which packages will be created. For example, you might want packages created for an entire level. Or, you might want packages created for sub-areas of a level. This setting depends on the hierarchy of how your building areas have been broken down under the Areas tab. Remember, your Deliverable Definition filter will determine which parts (Ex. Hangers, Pipe, Duct) are included in the package.
        
    4.  **Models** - A model must be associated with each Deliverable.
        

## Generate Project Deliverables

The **Projects > Deliverables** page is where Deliverables (project packages) are generated. Before generating packages, you can review the Area and Package Category, as well as the number of Parts and Assemblies that will be packaged.

**To generate Deliverables:**

1.  **Area Selection Filter** – Select project areas to be used for Deliverables. The filter displays the project and sub-areas in a hierarchical format as defined under Project > Areas. For each checked Area, when the Auto or Re-Generate Deliverables button is clicked, deliverables will be created for those areas. Use the **Deliverables without area checkbox** when the model parts did not have an area (Ex. Stratus.Part.BIMArea).
    
2.  **Generate Deliverables** - Click the **Generate Deliverables** button. The **Generate Deliverables** dialog will display. This dialog requires that you to limit the deliverables generated to the selected model(s), Deliverable Definitions and Package Category(s). Use the **Select All models** checkbox to quickly select all project models. Use the **Search** to search for a string in the model name, not the deliverable definition or the package category.
    
3.  Click **Continue** and the Deliverables will display by Model, Area, Name, and Package Category. In addition, information about the Parts, Assemblies, and Total Parts included for each package will display.
    
    1.  **Model** - The **model** associated with the deliverable will display.
        
    2.  **Area** - The **area** associated with the deliverable will display.
        
    3.  **Name** - The **deliverable definition** associated with the deliverable will display.
        
    4.  **Group** - The **group** is associated with Deliverable Definition Filter and the Filter's Grouping's Property Name under Admin > Company > Groupings.  Filters break out the packages and Groupings further break out packages by Property. 
        
    5.  **Package Category** - The **package category** selected for the deliverable under Project Deliverables Settings
        
    6.  **Package** - Package will initially be empty until a package is generated. 
        
    7.  **Required Date** - The **Required Date** will initially be empty until a package is generated. 
        
    8.  **Package Status** - Package Status will initially be empty until a package is generated. 
        
    9.  **Parts** - The number of loose parts in the deliverable.
        
    10.  **Assemblies** - The number of assemblies in the deliverable.
        
    11.  **Total Parts** - The number of total parts (loose parts + parts in assemblies) in the deliverable.
        

## Dismiss Warnings

Since a Project Deliverable combines a model, filter, and BIM area, when any of these are edited, a warning message displays alerting you to review the impact of changes on your Deliverables. The warning messages do not prevent you from using the Deliverables page. You can dismiss individual warning messages or click the **Dismiss all All Warnings** button.

## Manage Packages

One or more packages can be created and deleted from the Deliverables page.

## Select Deliverables

**To select deliverables, do one of the following:**

1.  **Click one or more checkboxes** - Click one or more checkboxes associated with each deliverable row. For example, with these 3 selected, the buttons to **Generate 3 Packages** or **Delete 3 Deliverables** become enabled.
    
2.  **Select All** - Click the **Select All** button to select all checkboxes. In this example, since 20 deliverables were generated, clicking **Select All** will enable the buttons to **Generate 20 Packages** or **Delete 3 Deliverables**. The **Clear Selection** will uncheck all checked boxes.
    

## Create One Package

**To create one package either select one row as described above, or:**

1.  Click the **Create a new Package** button 
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/34dac69d-7181-4b06-acc4-a1ccb75de8f0)
    
      in the Package column.
2.  **Package Creates** - The package will be created and automatically include:
    
    1.  **Package** - The **Package** name according to the Naming and Numbering configuration.
        
    2.  **Required** - The **Required** date 
        
    3.  **Package Status** - The **Package Status** will be the first Tracking Status where **Applies to Package** is checked.
        
3.  **Create Package** – Click the **Create New Package** button 
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/9d689163-7061-429c-b6a3-c2da3a296af3)
    
      to generate a package for the selected deliverable.  The Deliverable will convert into a package and as a result, the package will also display on the Packages > Dashboard (not shown).
4.  **Check Deliverable row** – Check the checkbox associated with the deliverable row and the options to **Generate # Packages** and **Delete # Deliverables** will display. Either click the Generate # Packages button to generate multiple packages or, click the Delete # Deliverables button to remove the selected deliverables from the Deliverables page. A deliverable can also be deleted by clicking the Delete button associated with the Deliverable.
    
5.  Once one or more packages have been created, the package(s) will display on the **Packages > Dashboard** and can follow the same workflow as other packages created from the Models > Viewer > Actions > Packages dialog.
    

## Generate Multiple Packages

To generate multiple packages, **select deliverable rows** as described above, or click the **Select All** button. In this example, **Select All** was clicked.

1.  Click the **Select All** button. All deliverables are selected.
    
2.  Click the **Generate 20 Packages** button. The packages will be created. 
    
    1.  **Note**: If any part or assembly included in the package generation process has a different Tracking Status, then the following message will display.
        

## Locked Package

1.  **Locked** - Once a package's tracking status has changed to where it is no longer in a Can Package tracking status, the **lock** icon displays indicating the package is in a tracking status that cannot be edited.
    

## Projects Deliverables Permissions

Permission the Project Deliverables page under Admin > Company > Project Roles > Projects > Deliverables.

1.  **Deliverables Settings** - When checked, the **Project Deliverable Settings** gear button on the Project Deliverables page which opens the Project Deliverable Settings edit dialog will display.
    
2.  **Viewer** - When unchecked, the **Project Deliverables** tab does not display.
    
3.  **Modify Deliverables** - When checked, the **Generate / Delete Deliverables** button will display on the Project Deliverables page.
    
4.  **Modify Packages** - When checked, the **Generate / Delete Packages** button will display on the Project Deliverables page.

## Stratus Academy

## Login

1.  To login to Stratus Academy, click the Stratus Academy link under Help. This link provides Single-Sign-On (SSO) access to the Stratus Academy portal. This is the only way Stratus users can access the **Stratus Academy**.
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/83e84ff3-30b6-488f-acb9-e52a2cceebec#media-blob-url=true&id=92b6aaa8-e9aa-4786-90e9-7c46efbcf3a2&collection=contentId-1999798273&contextId=1999798273&mimeType=image%2Fpng&name=image2024-8-22_15-23-14.png&size=39188&width=651&height=429&alt=)
    
2.  Once logged the Stratus Academy home page will display. 
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/1c1ece95-1260-4fa8-abf8-6339fabb755e#media-blob-url=true&id=80c98f78-90a9-4e08-b6a5-6cd95ec7e2e2&collection=contentId-1999798273&contextId=1999798273&mimeType=image%2Fpng&name=image2024-8-23_8-25-13.png&size=108481&width=1439&height=838&alt=)
    
3.  After the user is timed out of the portal or has clicked the Log Off button, the web page will be redirected to the Stratus > Help page.
    

## Customer Admin at Company

Some company’s choose to assign a person in the company to be their Stratus Academy Admin. This role can do the following:

-   Monitor their employees progress in taking courses, especially the Onboarding Hub > Stratus Fundamentals Certificate curriculum
    
-   View courses
    
-   View enrollments
    
-   View users list
    
-   Run reports on learner activity and progress, overall course activity and progress, and certificates
    

If you are a company admin for Stratus Academy, do the following to access the Admin tools:

1.  In Stratus under Help, click the Stratus Academy link which will log you into the Stratus Academy.
    
2.  Click the **Menu** and select **Admin**.
    
    ![image-20240828-155323.png](https://media-cdn.atlassian.com/file/26e2358d-3d5f-4741-9ac6-afde22c234c5/image/cdn?allowAnimated=true&client=5f4a70b1-9d9d-47c3-b388-87235680bb54&collection=contentId-1999798273&height=561&max-age=2592000&mode=full-fit&source=mediaCard&token=eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJpc3MiOiI1ZjRhNzBiMS05ZDlkLTQ3YzMtYjM4OC04NzIzNTY4MGJiNTQiLCJhY2Nlc3MiOnsidXJuOmZpbGVzdG9yZTpjb2xsZWN0aW9uOmNvbnRlbnRJZC0xOTk5Nzk4MjczIjpbInJlYWQiXX0sImV4cCI6MTc1MDg2ODEzOCwibmJmIjoxNzUwODY1MjU4fQ.Kitvb-808dtvvqPQHTjCUlFxzLWmrqNhBYDopt-qG3Q&width=760)
    
3.  The Admin Dashboard will display with the Admin tools highlighted.
    
    ![image-20240828-155517.png](https://media-cdn.atlassian.com/file/2894398d-15dd-4489-8b4b-0c21a38b0b7a/image/cdn?allowAnimated=true&client=5f4a70b1-9d9d-47c3-b388-87235680bb54&collection=contentId-1999798273&height=340&max-age=2592000&mode=full-fit&source=mediaCard&token=eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJpc3MiOiI1ZjRhNzBiMS05ZDlkLTQ3YzMtYjM4OC04NzIzNTY4MGJiNTQiLCJhY2Nlc3MiOnsidXJuOmZpbGVzdG9yZTpjb2xsZWN0aW9uOmNvbnRlbnRJZC0xOTk5Nzk4MjczIjpbInJlYWQiXX0sImV4cCI6MTc1MDg2ODEzOCwibmJmIjoxNzUwODY1MjU4fQ.Kitvb-808dtvvqPQHTjCUlFxzLWmrqNhBYDopt-qG3Q&width=941)

## Stratus Health

Receive critical email alerts and resolutions (Ex. Site down) by subscribing to the STRATUS Health system. 

1.  Click STRATUS Health link. The GTP Ecosystem Status page will display.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/342b2e41-5581-4d13-b8d3-72fb51fb6d89)
    
2.  Click the **Get Updates** button.
    
3.  Enter an email address and click Submit.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/baa7ba25-e5b7-4489-8dd1-b275d31d5663)
    
4.  You will receive new notifications.

# Jobsites - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Jobsites page is a management dashboard for each Station's work queue when the Station's Division is set to a Jobsite Division.

---
The Jobsites page is a management dashboard for each Station's work queue when the Station's Division is set to a Jobsite Division.  
![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/170819638/image2020-7-13_16-34-47.png?version=1&modificationDate=1594676088295&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=1195&height=250)

The Jobsites page enables a Shop Foreman role to manage queued items and send them to a tool on demand. Queued items include the number of Cut Lists, Point Lists, and/or Tasks for each package.

-   **Cut Lists** are generated from the Package's > Cut Lists tab.
-   **Point Lists** are generated from the Package's > Point Lists tab.
-   **Tasks** are generated from a package's Task Workflows.

**To access the Jobsites page:**

1.  Click the **Jobsites** menu item.  
    ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/170819638/image2019-9-18_14-38-34.png?version=1&modificationDate=1568835515480&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=895&height=322)
2.  Click the **Station** name to display when the queued item was requested, the project name, the package name, number of items and status.   
    ![](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/download/thumbnails/170819638/image2019-9-18_14-38-52.png?version=1&modificationDate=1568835533521&cacheVersion=1&api=v2&width=895&height=356)
3.  Information includes:
    1.  **Requested** \- The date/time the cut list was sent to the queue.
    2.  **Project** \- The cut list's project.
    3.  **Package** \- The cut list's package.
    4.  **Number of Items** \- The total number of items in the point list.
    5.  **Status** \- The status of the point list which is manually updated.
    6.  **Send to Tool** - Click the Send to Tool button to generate a downloadable CSV file and a DXF file.  The tool that items will be sent to is configured on either the package's Cut Lists or Point Lists page.

# Models Dashboard - STRATUS Knowledge Base - Confluence

> ## Excerpt
> The Models Dashboard provides basic information about each model.

---
The Models Dashboard provides basic information about each model.

-   1 [Summary](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/3277112/Models+Dashboard#Summary)
-   2 [Stratus Academy Course Video](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/3277112/Models+Dashboard#%5BhardBreak%5DStratus-Academy-Course-Video)
-   3 [CSG Webinar](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/3277112/Models+Dashboard#CSG-Webinar)
    -   3.1 [01/21/2021 CSG Webinar: STRATUS In-Depth Series, The Models Module (40:37)](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/3277112/Models+Dashboard#01%2F21%2F2021-CSG-Webinar%3A-STRATUS-In-Depth-Series%2C-The-Models-Module-(40%3A37))

## Summary

The Models Dashboard provides basic information about each model in a project including the type of model published (Revit or AutoCAD), the last published date/time, # of Packages, Parts, and Tasks, and the ability to delete the model. In addition, the Shipping Address used by the model can be edited.

1.  **Project** - The project where the model was published.
    
2.  **Model** - The name of the model published and a link to open the model in a separate tab. 
    
3.  **Type** - AutoCAD, Revit, CAMDuct.
    
4.  **Published** - The published date and time.
    
5.  **Conflict Resolution** - Overrides the conflict resolution for a model within a project.
    
6.  **Shipping Address** - Shipping Address applied in model reports that specify STRATUS.Model.ShippingAddress.xxx fields.
    
7.  **Publish Packages** - Select if the model will only be used to publish packages from CAMduct, ESTmep, FieldOrderz, and PypeServer.
    
8.  **Version** - Refers to the BIM 360 model version.
    
9.  **#Packages** - The total number of packages in the model.
    
10.  **#Assemblies** - The total number of assemblies in the model.
    
11.  **#Parts** - The total number of parts in the model.
    
12.  **#Tasks** - The total number of tasks in the model.
    
13.  **Run Report**
    
    1.  Click the **Run Report** icon.
        
    2.  The  “Generate Report” dialog will display. Select a report and click the **Generate Report** button.
        
    3.  A new browser tab will open and will display the report.
        
14.  **Delete** 
    
    1.  Click the **Delete** icon.
        
    2.  The "Delete Model and Data" dialog similar to the following will display and will include the name of the model to be permanently deleted noting that all related data associated with the model including assemblies, packages, etc. will be deleted.
        
    3.  Click **Delete Model and Data** to delete.
        

##   
Stratus Academy Course Video

To take the Task Definitions course, login to [**Stratus Academy**](https://academy.stratus.build/ "https://academy.stratus.build/") and locate the course **MGR-301: Admin 1 - Models Overview**.

## Open a Model in the Models > Viewer

There are several ways to open a model in the Models> Viewer.

## Open a Model in the Models > Viewer

1.  Click the Models tab. If the Viewer tab is not set as the default tab, click Viewer.
    
2.  The Project and Model last used will display.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/e896726b-4963-4098-934a-c15909f8f7d0)
    

## Open a Model from the Models > Dashboard

1.  Click the Models tab. If the Dashboard tab is not set as the default tab, click Dashboard.
    
2.  Select the Project. The list of the Project's models will display.
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/87c7890a-398d-4497-94ed-e009d4af989f)
    
3.  Click the name of the Model to open the model in a separate browser tab.
    

## Open a Model from the Packages > Dashboard

1.  Go to the Packages > Dashboard.
    
2.  Click the Model name to open the model in the Models > Viewer. **Note**: In this example, the Default Report is displaying. 
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/e8379774-dea0-4203-b21e-13ea4867e268)
    

## Open Package from the Containers > Dashboard

Once a package has been added to a container, it will display under Containers > Dashboard.

1.  From the Containers > Dashboard, expand a Container to which a package has been added.
    
2.  Click the model name to open the model in a separate browser window. 
    
3.  The model will display with the Project and Model selected. 
    

## Models Viewer Navigation

## View

During the model publish process, a **Default 3D View** will be selected. This view will display in the Models > Viewer. For users who have permission, the View can be manually changed in Stratus. The View drop-down can display different published views. When a 2D View is selected, the Stratus Toolbar is disabled.

![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/0ecba615-ae42-4409-ab71-51f7eb3613ba)

## Selected Part Tracking Status

When parts are selected in the Models > Viewer, their Tracking Status and number will display. For example:

1.  **Selected Parts have the same Tracking Status** - When the selected parts have the same tracking status (Ex. Packaged), the tracking status and the number of parts (Ex. 3) selected will display.
    
2.  **Selected Parts have different Tracking Status** - When the selected parts have different tracking status (Ex. Design), the tracking status’s and the number of parts selected (Ex. 1) in each will display.
    
3.  **Note**: For tablet users or those running in mobile mode, this feature is not supported. The hamburger icon displays when in mobile mode.
    

## Models Viewer Settings

Click the gear icon to access the viewer's **Settings**. See the [**Viewer Settings and Search**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/2011136001 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/2011136001") article for more information.  

![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/2040bb32-94a2-49e3-9f55-9ef7ce757c37)

Settings in the Models > Viewer include the following:

-   **Hidden Parts Shaded**
    
-   **Assembly Selection**
    
-   **Multiple Part Selection**
    
-   **Dynamic Tags**
    
-   **Decimal Inches / Feet Inches Toggle**
    

## Viewer Search for Parts, Assemblies, and Packages

Click the Search icon to access viewer **Search**. See the [**Viewer Settings and Search**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/2011136001 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/2011136001") article for more information.

The Stratus Model Viewer Toolbar includes some handy tools. The Stratus Toolbar is also used on the Packages > Viewer and the Assemblies > Viewer. Unless specified, the tools function the same across all viewers.

## Display Modes

1.  **Display Modes** – Model parts can be color coded by several modes including Areas, Assemblies, Categories, Containers, Packages, Tracking, and Purchasing. Click **Normal** to return to a non-color coded display mode.  Displays Modes also work when Stratus Toolbar > Filters have been applied in the Viewer. Only items that include parts display in the results.
    
    1.  **Parts** 
        
        1.  Each mode displays information about the total number and percent of parts in these categories. Any filters applied to the view will impact these values. Below is an example where Display Mode is set to Areas.
            
    2.  **Regions**
        
        1.  A Region is a 3d polygon outline over the full region. For Regions to display, BIM Areas must be defined for the model.  In this example, there are Revit Rotated Scope Boxes.  
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/7a9cfd3b-2862-4ea6-8cfd-da1f5f16a201)
            
        2.  After the model is publish and BIM Areas defined, the scope boxes display within Regions.
            

## Filters

### Company Filter Cache

To improve performance, Company filters are cached on the server. 

Caching is initiated by the first user who opens the Filters > Company dialog. As a result, the first user to open Filters > Company in a model will notice the time it takes to calculate all the filters. Subsequently, users who open Filters > Company for the model will notice that the filters display within seconds. The Filters > Company cache will be purged and recalculated each time any of the following occurs, and, as a result, the first user to load the viewer webpage and open Filters > Company will wait for the recalculation to repopulate the cache.

Filters > Company will purge and recalculate after any of the following events:

-   When a Company **Filter** is edited under Admin > Company > Filters where Model Viewer is checked.
    
-   When an **Alias**, **Field**, or **Grouping** that is directly referenced by a company filter is modified.
    
-   The **Refresh** link is clicked at the bottom of the Filters > Company dialog.
    
-   The model has been republished.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/dc392a7e-fc5e-4529-a66f-780af669ba45)
    

### Filter Descriptions

1.  Filters are used to slice and dice the model the way you want to view it. Filters include:
    
    1.  **Areas** – Areas can be imported from the model or manually entered by the Stratus Admin.  See the [**Areas (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742") article for how to configure areas from the model.
        
    2.  **Assemblies** – An assembly can be defined in the model or within Stratus under Actions.
        
    3.  **Categories** – Cost Categories are defined by the Stratus Admin.
        
    4.  **Company** – Company filters can be configured by the Stratus Admin. Filter categories will not display when no parts match the filter.
        
    5.  **Containers** - Packages, Assemblies, and Parts added to a Container display in the Containers filter. See the [**Containers Assign**](http://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151 "http://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1877574151") article for more information. The Containers Filter displays a tree structure broken out by Container Type and then containers. In this example, there are 2 Container Types, Cart and Truck. There are 2 trucks and the Container page for Truck B displays on the right. Notice that a container can include elements from different projects and models, but the Filters > Container in the viewer will only display elements within the selected model.
        
    6.  **Levels** – Levels are automatically brought in from the Revit model or AutoCAD drawing.
        
    7.  **Packages** 
        
        1.  Packages are defined in Stratus under Actions.
            
        2.  **Package Category Filter toggle option**  - Because parts may exist in more than one package, so long as the package is in a different Package Category, the filter is flexible in how it works. The toggle applies a rule that say ALL the checked boxes, or, ANY of the checked boxes apply.  
            
        3.  In this Packages toggle example the **Show Parts For All Selection** option is checked. Parts are visible because they exist in any checked package.
            
        4.  In this Packages toggle example the **Filter Parts Across Categories** option is checked. Parts are hidden because they don't exist in packages selected in both categories. 
            
        5.  In addition, the filter includes information about the number of parts in the currently selected view. Some parts are "**Unassigned Parts**" which means they have not yet been assigned to a package, and some parts are "**not in view**" which means the parts cannot display because they are not in the selected view. You would need to switch to the view that contains those parts in order to view them.
            
    8.  **Systems** – Systems are automatically brought in from the Revit model or AutoCAD drawing and breaks out your services by material and size.
        
    9.  **Tracking** – Company tracking statuses are configured by the Stratus Admin.
        
        1.  **Date Range option**
            
            1.  The date range option can be used to run reports for KPIs. For example, it can be used to display all items that have changed to the “Fabricated” status in the last month. All Tracking statuses are displayed in the list even if they do not have matching parts in the viewer. To use the date range under Filters > Tracking:
                
            2.  By default, the Tracking date range option is disabled and unchecked.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/41c53ba7-579d-443d-8b19-235952cba2e0)
                
            3.  Click the **Changes** checkbox to enable the feature.
                
                1.  All tracking statuses will be displayed in the list since dates change, different parts can be included and the counts for each will also update.
                    
                2.  By default, the date range end date is set for today and the start date is set for 30 days in the past.
                    
            4.  Set the dates as needed.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/5d50643d-f243-4399-92a2-d29b6380ac62)
                
            5.  Hover over either date to display the number of days, including the end date, that are in the date range.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/20a27f76-f827-4614-a8f3-c962715b8077)
                
            6.  Disable the Tracking date range option by unchecking the Changes checkbox.
                
    10.  **References**
        
        1.  References filters linked to models or xrefs published along with the primary model. In Revit, a specific view (based on the Publish Settings) may be selected for background viewing.  If the selected view does not include a 3D view, a message will display.
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/9b46e0e8-66ef-4263-8a23-68a27c1eb0d5)
            
        2.  The References filter includes **Clip Settings** within all of the viewers (Models, Packages, and Assemblies).
            
            1.  **Default Clip Settings** - The default **Clip Settings** for Bottom, Top, Left, Right, Front, and Back will be different for every assembly, package, and model because they are based on the bounding box for the isolated parts in each.
                
            2.  **Viewer Preferences** - Saved Clip Settings changes will only be applied automatically on page refresh when Account Settings > Profile > Viewer Preference are checked.  
                
                ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/5ec5a092-eaaf-4b22-a647-63236a785033)
                
            3.  To **Save** **Clip Settings** changes after making changes (**Example: Assemblies > Viewer**):
                
                1.  In the Assemblies > Viewer, open the **References** tool. The **Clip Settings** and **References** display.
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/e81777e0-a3d9-405d-a794-ddfc9b75dc88)
                    
                2.  Select a Reference (Ex. **ReferencePipe.rvt**) and it will display.
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/aa4a6d86-b0f4-4521-ab38-bfc15a816c63)
                    
                3.  Edit the **Clip Settings**. In the example below, the Right **Clip Setting** was checked and the value changed from -47.83 to -55. This change is not yet saved.
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/d2687057-2189-4dcf-92f5-c0a9084a8741)
                    
                4.  Click the **Save the current selection for this view of the model** button. The **Save Settings** dialog will display. Notice that the confirmation dialog displays to let you know that the change is applied when any user open this assembly in the viewer. Click **Ok** to save the changes. Like other Filters, changes to References are applied to the Stratus Sheet and Attachments > Reports.
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/5dd69db9-37ed-4040-9971-d7ba57fa0054)
                    
            4.  To **Reset Clip Settings**:
                
                1.  In the Assemblies > Viewer, open the **References** tool. The **Clip Settings** and **References** display.
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/8ee4417c-aa92-4412-8cd6-36fb49c7d937)
                    
                2.  Click the **Reset the model clipping values to extents of visible parts** button. The **Clip Settings** values will revert to their original clip values (Ex. Right = -47.83). Any checked **Clip Settings** (Ex. Right) or checked **References** (Ex. ReferencePipe.rvt 3D) will remain checked. Click **Save** to save changes. Otherwise, refreshing the page will revert back to the previously saved values (Ex. -55).
                    
                    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/026a5ae0-7a19-41d1-9f05-5fddd3302ae5)
                    
2.  **Filters search window - apply to results button**
    
    1.  The Filters search window and apply a results button applies to all filters.  Users can **enter a search** such as “Water” under the Systems filter which filters the tree list down to only systems that include “Water” in them.  A **Check Search Results** button appears to the right of the search text box and when clicked it toggles the checkbox selection for each item displayed in the tree that matches the search criteria.
        
        Below are some examples:
        
3.  **Filters – Areas Cascade Checkbox**
    
    1.  Under Models > Viewer > Filter by Area, there are cascading checkboxes that enable you to:
        
        1.  Select all areas within the level.
            
        
        3.  Select children areas independent of the parent.
            

### Filter Loading from Account Settings > Viewer Preferences

Each user’s last set of filters per model are stored. Filters for the Models Viewer are separate from the Packages Viewer filters. Each user can configure whether they want last session filters to be automatically or manually applied.

To configure last session filters to be applied automatically under **Account Settings > Viewer Preferences:**

-   See the [**Viewer Preferences**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1953858294/Profile#View-Preferences "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/1953858294/Profile#View-Preferences") article for more information on how to configure these Viewer Preferences.
    
-   See the [**Automatically Load Last Session Filter Settings**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/9043969#ModelsViewer-AutomaticallyLoadLastSessionFilterSettings "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/9043969#ModelsViewer-AutomaticallyLoadLastSessionFilterSettings") example below on how these settings are applied in the viewers.
    

To manually apply last session filters using the **Load Last** button within the Filters dialog, see the [**Manually Load Last Session Filter Settings**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/9043969#ModelsViewer-ManuallyLoadLastSessionFilterSettings "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/9043969#ModelsViewer-ManuallyLoadLastSessionFilterSettings") example below. 

#### Manually Load Last Session Filter Settings

The following example is for the Models Viewer, however, the Packages Viewer works the same.

When **Models Viewer** is unchecked under **Account Settings > Viewer Preferences,** Model filter settings will not be automatically applied when a viewer opens. Because the filter setting change for each model and the packages within the model are always stored, they can be manually applied at any time by clicking the **Load Last** button in the Filters panel.

Below is the filter behavior when **Account Settings > Viewer Preferences > Models Viewer** is unchecked under **Apply last session filter settings.** 

1.  When the Viewer > Filter is opened, the filter settings will be **Off** since no filters will have been applied.
    
2.  If filters have previously been applied, click the **Load Last** button.
    
    1.  The **last session Model filter settings** will be applied. See below for more information.
        
3.  When the user checks a filter:
    
    1.  The individual filter will be checked and actively applied to the viewer.
        
    2.  The Filter Group will be **On.**
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
        
    5.  This is the **last session Model filter settings** which is stored. If filters had already been checked, then this new filter will be added to the **last session Model filter settings**.
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/18cff9ab-28d0-4308-b88e-9bf2536dd077)
        
4.  If the user unchecks a filter:
    
    1.  The individual filter will be unchecked and no longer applied to the viewer.
        
    2.  The Filter Group will be **On** unless there are no remaining individual filters within the Filter Group in which case the Filter Group button will be **Off**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On** unless there are no remaining filters in which case the All Filter Group button will be **Off**.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue unless there are no remaining filters in which case the Filters button will not be highlighted.
        
    5.  This is the **last session Model filter settings** which is stored.  
        A browser session is restarted by one of the following
        
    6.  Refresh the page.
        
    7.  Change to a different Model.
        
    8.  Change to a different Model View within the same model.
        
    9.  Close/open the web browser.
        
    10.  Click **Clear All Filters** and then click **Load Last.**
        
5.  When a browser session is restarted (see above):
    
    1.  All individual filters will be unchecked and no longer applied to the viewer.
        
    2.  All Filter Groups will be **Off**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **Off**.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will not be highlighted blue.
        
    5.  The **last session Model filter settings** are still stored. As a result, the **Load Last** button is enabled.
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/74e7e23a-1f4c-4abe-a88f-77c634c1e605)
        
6.  To load the user’s **last session Model filter settings**, click the **Load Last** button. The **last session Model filter settings** will be applied.
    
    1.  The **last session Model filter settings will be applied**, individual filters will be checked, and filters will actively filter the viewer.
        
    2.  Filter Groups were turned On will be **On**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
        
    5.  The **Loading filters …** message will display while the last saved filter settings (both Areas and Systems) are being applied to the Models Viewer.
        
    6.  The **Load Last** button will be disabled.
        
    7.  The **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
        
7.  If the user turns a Filter Group **Off**, and in this example, there are 2 active filter groups:
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/b938564c-53d4-4c3a-89a2-6a12a7e3be09)
    
    1.  The individual filters within the turned Off Filters Group will be checked but they will not be actively filtering the viewer.
        
    2.  Filter Groups that were turned off are **Off**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On** since in this example there is one Filter Group still active.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
        
    5.  The **Load Last** button will be disabled.
        
    6.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
        
    7.  **Note:** A filter group must be turned back on in order for the individual filters to filter the viewer.
        
8.  If the user turns **Off** all filter groups, the model is unfiltered. All Filter Groups can be turned off by either a) manually clicking **Off** for each Filter Group or b) by clicking the All Filter Group button to **Off**.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/97d2a943-c1a7-4da4-8938-9914990e26bf)
    
    1.  The individual filters within the turned Off Filters Group will remain checked but they will not be actively filtering the viewer.
        
    2.  Filter Groups that were turned off are **Off**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **Off** since all Filters Groups have been turned off.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will not be highlighted blue once the Filters dialog is closed.
        
    5.  The **Load Last** button will be disabled until the browser is refreshed.
        
    6.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
        
9.  To filter the parts again after Filter Groups have been turned Off, the user can:
    
    1.  Refresh the page.
        
    2.  Click the **Load Last** button. The viewer will not be filtered until a Filter Group is turned on.
        
    3.  Click the Filter Group **On** button for one or more **Filter Groups** that were set to **Off**.
        
        1.  Each Filter Group that is turned will filter the model.
            
        2.  Individual filters will be checked and will actively filter the viewer.
            
        3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
            
        4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
            
        5.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
            
10.  **To clear all filters including individually checked filters:**
    
    1.  Click the **Clear All Filters** button:
        
    2.  The page will load with the following:
        
    3.  The individual filters within the turned Off Filters Group will be unchecked and will not actively filter the viewer.
        
    4.  Filter Groups will be turned **Off**.
        
    5.  The All Filter Group button will be **Off**.
        
    6.  The Filters button in the toolbar will not be highlighted blue once the Filters dialog is closed.
        
    7.  The **Load Last** button will be enabled.
        
    8.  The **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are still stored.
        
        1.  **Note**: If after clicking the **Clear All Filters** button the user edits one or more filters, then the new **last session Model filter settings** will be the cumulative filter edits since the Clear All Filters button was clicked.
            
11.  To load the **last session Model filter settings**, click **Load Last**.
    
    1.  The **last session Model filter settings will be applied,** individual filters will be checked, and filters will actively filter the viewer.
        
    2.  Filter Groups that were turned on will be **On**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
        
    5.  The **Loading filters …** message will display while the last saved filter settings (both Areas and Systems) are being applied to the Models Viewer.
        
    6.  The **Load Last** button will be disabled.
        
    7.  The **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
        

#### Automatically Load Last Session Filter Settings

When **Account Settings > Viewer Preferences >** **Apply last session filter settings > Models Viewer** is checked Model filter settings will be automatically applied when a viewer opens.

Below is the filter behavior when Account Viewer Preferences are checked for **Apply last session filter settings** for **Model Viewer**. The Models Viewer is used as an example, but the same behavior occurs in the Packages Viewer when the **Apply last session filter settings** for **Packages Viewer** is checked.

1.  When the Models > Viewer is opened:
    
    1.  The **Loading filters …** message will display while the last saved filter settings (both Areas and Systems) are being applied to the Models Viewer.
        
    2.  When the Model is done loading its **last session Model filter settings** will filter the model.
        
2.  Open Filters to review and edit filters:
    
    1.  The **last session Model filter settings** display.
        
    2.  The individually checked filters will be checked and filtering the viewer.
        
    3.  Filter Groups that were on will be **On**.
        
    4.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
        
    5.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
        
3.  Check and uncheck individual filters as needed. Any changes will be automatically stored as the new **last session Model filter settings**.
    
4.  If the user turns a Filter Group **Off**, and in this example, there are 2 active filter groups:
    
    1.  The individual filters within the turned Off Filters Group will be checked but they will not be actively filtering the viewer.
        
    2.  Filter Groups that were turned off are **Off**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On** since in this example there is one Filter Group still active.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
        
    5.  The **Load Last** button will be disabled.
        
    6.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
        
    7.  **Note:** A filter group must be turned back on in order for the individual filters to filter the viewer.
        
5.  If the user turns **Off** all filter groups, the model is unfiltered. All Filter Groups can be turned off by either a) manually clicking **Off** for each Filter Group or b) by clicking the All Filter Group button to **Off**.
    
    1.  The individual filters within the turned Off Filters Group will remain checked but they will not be actively filtering the viewer.
        
    2.  Filter Groups that were turned off are **Off**.
        
    3.  The All Filter Group button will be **Off** since all Filters Groups have been turned off.
        
    4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will not be highlighted blue once the Filters dialog is closed.
        
    5.  The **Load Last** button will be disabled until the browser is refreshed.
        
    6.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
        
6.  To filter the parts again after Filter Groups have been turned Off, the user can:
    
    1.  Open Filters.
        
    2.  Click the Filter Group **On** button for one or more **Filter Groups** that were set to **Off**.
        
        1.  Each Filter Group that is turned will filter the model.
            
        2.  Individual filters will be checked and will actively filter the viewer.
            
        3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
            
        4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
            
        5.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
            
7.  **To clear all filters including individually checked filters:**
    
    1.  Click the **Clear All Filters** button:
        
    2.  The page will load with the following:
        
    3.  The individual filters within the turned Off Filters Group will be unchecked and will not actively filter the viewer.
        
    4.  Filter Groups will be turned **Off**.
        
    5.  The All Filter Group button will be **Off**.
        
    6.  The Filters button in the toolbar will not be highlighted blue once the Filters dialog is closed.
        
    7.  The **Load Last** button will be enabled.
        
    8.  The **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are still stored.
        
        1.  **Note**: If after clicking the **Clear All Filters** button the user edits one or more filters, then the new **last session Model filter settings** will be the cumulative filter edits since the Clear All Filters button was clicked.
            
    9.  Click the Filter Group **On** button for one or more **Filter Groups** that were set to **Off**.
        
        1.  Each Filter Group that is turned will filter the model.
            
        2.  Individual filters will be checked and will actively filter the viewer.
            
        3.  The All Filter Group button will be **On**.
            
        4.  The Filters button in the toolbar will be highlighted blue.
            
        5.  The new **last session Model filter settings** including the Filter Groups **On/Off** setting are stored.
            

## Actions

Actions are ways to work with the model outside the modeling tool. You can add/subtract model items to/from Areas, Assemblies, Categories, Packages, Containers, and Tracking. You can also view an attachment for a model item. And, you can run a report on model items. Actions include:

### Areas

1.  **Areas**  – The **Areas** action enables you to add or remove parts from an Area.  The Areas available in the drop-down list reflect project areas configured under Projects > Areas and clicking the Import Areas button. This action imports the areas from the selected model. See the [**Areas (Admin)**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/103284742") article for more information.
    
    1.  To add a part to an area using this tool, click the **Areas** action.
        
    2.  **To add items**
        
        1.  **Click the drop-down** to select the target Area to add the parts.
            
        2.  **Item selection (in the model)**
            
            1.  **Click** – will select one item.
                
            2.  **Click + Shift** will select all clicked items. If an item is an assembly, the entire assembly will be selected.
                
            3.  **Click + Ctrl** will select all clicked items. If an item is an assembly, only the item clicked will be selected, not the whole assembly.
                
            4.  Click the **Window Select** button in the Stratus toolbar and then window select the parts you want to be selected.
                
        3.  **Add selection**
            
            1.  **\+ Add Selected** \- Click this button to add parts that were selected using any of the Item selection methods (above) to the selected Area.
                
            2.  **\+ Add Visible** – Click this button to add parts that are visible in the Model Viewer through the Stratus filters to the selected Area. 
                
            3.  **Auto Assign Areas** - Click this button to auto-assign visible parts to different areas based on property data that identifies the area for each part.
                
    3.  **To remove items**
        
        1.  **Follow the steps above and then:**
            
            1.  **\- Remove Selected** \-  Click this button to remove parts that were selected using any of the Item selection methods (above) to the selected Area.
                
            2.  **\- Remove Visible** - Click this button to remove parts that are visible in the Model Viewer through the Stratus filters to the selected Area.
                

### Assemblies

1.  **Assemblies** - See the [**Create and Manage Assemblies**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/65634315") article for information. 
    

### Attachments

1.  **Attachments** - You can view attachments to a part, assembly, or package. An attachment can be:
    
    1.  a file attached to a part that is accessible to Stratus after the publish processes.
        
    2.  a document or image that was attached to a part, assembly, or package using Stratus.
        

### Categories

1.  **Categories** - Categories or Cost Categories are configured by your company Admin under Admin > Company > Categories. These categories can be assigned to any part selected or isolated in the model.
    

### Containers

The Models Viewer and Packages Viewer includes the **Actions > Containers** dialog to provide the ability to add/remove items (parts, assemblies, and packages) to/from a container.

#### Assign Permission

**To assign permission to use this feature:**

1.  Go to Admin > Company > Project Roles.
    
    1.  **Models Viewer** - Select Models > Viewer > Actions > Containers
        
    2.  **Packages Viewer** - Select Packages > Details > Viewer > Toolbar > Actions > Containers
        

#### Select or Filter Items in the Viewer

Items (Parts, Assemblies, Packages) can either be selected (highlighted in the viewer) or filtered (visible) in the viewer.

-   To **select** (highlight in the viewer) a part, assembly, or package, use Window Select or Select Connected tool, or via a Click, Ctrl-Click, and Shift-Click.
    
-   To **filter** (not highlighted but visible in the viewer) a part, assembly, or package in the viewer, use a Stratus filter.
    
-   The **Add Assemblies** checkbox, when checked, provides a way to select a part within an assembly and add the entire assembly to the Container.
    

**To select items in the viewer to Add/Remove To/From a Container:**

1.  **Selected** - Select any item(s). Actions buttons remain disabled until a Container is selected.
    
    1.  Once a Container is selected all 4 action buttons will be enabled (Ex. **Add Selected**, **Remove Selected**, **Add Visible**, **Remove Visible**). **Note:** Add/Remove Visible buttons can still be used, but these commands are not limited to the selected (highlighted) parts.
        
2.  **Filter Visible** \- When a filter is used and no items are selected in the viewer. The filtered items are visible.
    
    1.  Once a Container is selected only the **Add Visible** and **Remove Visible** buttons are enabled since no parts have been selected.
        
3.  **Select Items in Container**
    
    1.  When an item is selected that is already in a container, the Container Type and Container name will display.
        
    2.  If multiple parts are selected and belong to different containers, only the container of the first selected item will be displayed.
        

#### Actions > Containers Summary

Below are definitions of the Action > Containers options:

1.  **Container Type** - To filter containers, select **Container Type**.
    
2.  **Container (Required)** - A list of all company containers displays and can be filtered by the selected **Container Type**. Select a container to add/remove items.
    
    1.  **Add Assemblies (checkbox)**
        
        1.  **Checked (default)** \- When **Add Assemblies** is checked, if any part selected in the viewer is also included in an assembly, then the entire assembly will be added to the container when any of the Add/Remove buttons are clicked.
            
        2.  **Unchecked** \- When **Add Assemblies** is unchecked, individual assembly parts can be added to a container.
            
            1.  In this example, the selected part is also included in an assembly and Add Selected is clicked.
                
            2.  Even though the part belongs to an assembly, only the selected part will be added to the container when Add/Remove Selected buttons are clicked.
                
3.  **Add Selected** - After selecting items in the viewer, click the **Add Selected** button to add the selected items to the selected container. Visible items not selected will not be added.
    
4.  **Remove Selected** - After selecting items in the viewer, click the **Remove Selected** button to remove the selected items from the selected container. Visible items not selected will not be removed.
    
5.  **Add Visible** \- Any part that displays in the viewer is Visible. **Note**: If the **Hidden Parts Shaded** tool is checked, those hidden parts are not considered visible. Use filters as needed to isolate items to be added to a container. Click the **Add Visible** button to add the items to the selected container.
    
    1.  **Note**: Only the visible parts of a package will be added to the container, not the entire package if it is not visible or included in the View.
        
6.  **Remove Visible** \- Any part that displays in the viewer is Visible. **Note**: If the **Hidden Parts Shaded** tool is checked, those hidden parts are not considered visible. Use filters as needed to isolate items to be removed from a container. Click the **Remove Visible** button to remove the items from the selected container.
    
    1.  **Note**: Only the visible parts of a package will be removed, not the entire package if it is not visible or included in the View.
        

#### Example: Add Selected Items to a Container

1.  Select items to be added to a container. All Actions buttons remain disabled until a Container is selected.
    
2.  Select a **Container (Required)** - A list of all company containers displays and can be filtered by the selected **Container Type**. Once a container has been selected, the action buttons will be enabled.
    
3.  Click the **Add Selected** button. The selected items will be added to the container under Containers > Assign. A Tracking row will be automatically added and include the Comment “Stratus Added”.
    

#### Example: Add Visible Items to a Container

1.  Filter to items to be added to a container. In this example, the filtered package includes an assembly and loose parts. All Actions buttons remain disabled until a Container is selected.
    
2.  Select a **Container (Required)** - A list of all company containers displays and can be filtered by the selected **Container Type**. Once a container has been selected, the Actions buttons will be enabled. Since no items were selected, the **Add Selected** button remains disabled.
    
3.  **Click the Add Visible** button. The visible items will be added to the container under Containers > Assign. A Tracking row will be automatically added and include the Comment “Stratus Added”.
    
    1.  By expanding the Package, the 2 assemblies and loose parts display.
        

#### Example: Remove Selected

Parts, assemblies, and packages can be removed from a container individually or as a whole.

1.  Using the previous **Example: Add Visible Items to a Container**, select items to be removed from a container. In this example, all loose parts were selected.
    
2.  **Remove Selected** - After selecting items in the viewer, click the **Remove Selected** button to remove the items from the selected container. Only the assemblies remain.
    

#### Example: Remove Visible

1.  Using the previous **Example: Add Visible Items to a Container**, filter to an assembly to be removed from a container and selected the Container. **Note**: When **Hidden Parts Shaded** is checked, the hidden parts are not considered “Visible” so using the Add/Remove Visible button will not impact those items.
    
2.  Under Containers > Assign, the visible assembly has been removed.
    

#### Example: Move Items From Selected Container

1.  If a selected item is already included in a Container and the user attempts to add it to a different container, a “**Move items from selected container?”** message similar to the following will display where the user can **Cancel** or **Move** the parts from one container to the other.
    

### Packages

1.  **Packages** - See the [**Create Packages**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/67502081 "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/67502081") article for information about creating a package. 
    

### Reports

1.  **Reports** - Reports, including CSV table reports, PDF formatted reports, and ZPL label reports are configured by your company admin. Once run, they will either display in a separate tab or be downloaded to your computer. A report can be run on:
    
    1.  **Run for Selected** - Limits the report data to the selected parts in the current view. This option will be disabled if no parts have been selected.
        
    2.  **Run for Visible** - Limits the report data to the visible parts in the current view. 
        
    3.  **Entire Model** - Generates report data for all parts in the model regardless of the view.
        

### Tracking

1.  **Tracking** - This is one way to apply a tracking status to a part, assembly, or package. If applying a new tracking status to isolated parts in a model, if a package or assembly has been isolated so that all its parts are visible, the tracking status change will be applied to the package’s or assembly’s log as appropriate. To change a tracking status:
    
    1.  Selecting the part, assembly, or package in the model
        
    2.  Selecting the target tracking status (Design below)
        
    3.  Selecting a Division (Detailing below)
        
    4.  Optionally adding information like a comment, hours, cost type, and/or cost
        
    5.  and then applying the information to the items that have either been **Selected** or **Isolated** (using Filters) 
        

## Grid Offset Measurement

1.  For a digital tape measure, click the **Grid Offset Measurement** tool and then select an item in the model. The tool will display the item’s dimension offset from grid line intersections. You can pick which level the tool is referencing and select which grid to measure in the drop-down. The distance to the X, Y grid line will display for point A and point B.
    

## Display Grid

1.  The **Display Grid** button shows the grids from the model or a Revit referenced model (see below). 
    
    1.  **Note**: Lines, in general, are only visible within the Stratus model viewer if you have the Forge viewer setting to "Display lines" toggled on.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/c6018db4-2665-4682-9b77-a0526ee9596d)
        
2.  The grid displays at the elevation of the selected part.
    
3.  The grid intersection annotation includes a dash separator to better represent the individual grid values.
    
4.  The grid can be used from a reference model. To use this feature:
    
    1.  In the Publish dialog, check the **Include References** checkbox.
        
    2.  In a Stratus Viewer, under **References**, check the model that includes the grid.
        
    3.  The **Grid Offset Measurement** tool will work as well.
        

## Window Select

The **Window Select** tool behaves differently depending on how you click and drag the mouse.

1.  Before each attempt to Window Select, make sure the button is enabled. 
    
2.  **Click and drag left to right** \- When the **Window Select** tool is drawn from left to right, parts are selected when the are within the bounds of the selecting box.
    
3.  **Click and drag right to left** - When the **window selection** tool is drawn from right to left, parts are selected when the selecting box touches the part.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/d24854c8-4de1-4329-8469-8f995fa5b69c)
    

## Select Connected

1.  The **Select Connected** command selects all items connected to the selected item or range of items. In addition to being a fast selection tool, using either the Select Connected or Window Select commands will ensure that small parts like welds and olets are selected. Only parts that are in the selected view or filter will be included when Selected Connected is clicked. As a result, parts that are not in the selected view or filter but are connected to a part that is in the view or filter, will not be selected. Select Connected can be used as a filter to create an assembly or package. For example:
    
    1.  **Select one part and then click Selected Connected** to select all connected parts.
        
    2.  To select a run range, click the first part, **hold down the Ctrl key** and select the last part. Everything in between will be selected.
        
    3.  You can also **select branches** by clicking a part in this branch, click the Tee, click the part on this run, and then click the **Select Connected** button.
        
    4.  Or, if you want to select multiple runs, click the first and last parts on this run, click the first and last parts on another run, and then click the **Select Connect** button.
        
    5.  In this case, all of the conduits at the end of a bank of conduit runs have been selected.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/13a9fb96-c0ca-4f62-82cc-9882ddc1bca3)
        
    6.  Click **Select Connected** has the effect of grabbing all of the downstream parts.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/ba7bce59-687f-4131-8b07-d45b980b831b)
        
    7.  In this case, the ends of two different spools have been connected.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/54a58cb9-492f-48b7-b76b-a9b7e6584762)
        
    8.  Click **Select Connected** has the effect of grabbing all of the parts between the selected parts.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/7b812c1b-f161-4157-9a15-5b4ece45e9f8)
        
    9.  Once parts are selected, you can execute any of the commands under Actions like add selected parts to an assembly or package, change tracking status, run a report and more.
        

## Properties

The **Properties** tool displays the properties of one or more selected parts from the Revit or AutoCAD database. This tool is available in all viewers.

1.  To display item properties, click the **Properties** button and an item from the viewer. Depending on each user's settings, property values captured from the model will display. 
    
2.  **Parts Selected** - The number of parts selected in the viewer displays. **Note**: Part Template links will be provided for each part selected.
    
3.  **All Properties** - Checkbox toggles the display from the Display Template, if any, to All Properties.
    
    1.  **Unchecked** - When Unchecked, only the properties whose Visible option is checked under Admin > Company > Part Templates > Template (selected) > Properties will display. See the **Visible** section of the [**Configure Part Properties**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/217809750/Part+Templates+Admin#Configure-Part-Properties "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/217809750/Part+Templates+Admin#Configure-Part-Properties") article for more information.
        
    2.  **Checked** - When Checked, all Properties will display in alphabetic order. If Hide Empty Values is checked, then those properties will not display.
        
    3.  **Note:** The setting will persist after the is page refreshed.
        
4.  **Hide Empty Values** - Hides properties that have blank values.
    
    1.  **Unchecked** \- Allows the display of properties that have blank values
        
    2.  **Checked** \- Prevents the display of properties that have blank values.
        
    3.  **Note:** The setting will persist after the is page refreshed.
        
5.  **Template Name** - The Template Name is the name of the part template for the selected part. The **Template Name** is linked to the Admin > Company > Part Templates page for the selected part where its properties, including its **Visible** and Item **Number settings** can be edited. When clicked, the Part Templates page will display in a separate window and the Parts Search will be filled with the template name. Select the part template to display Properties. **Permission**: The Template Name only displays for users who have been assigned a **Company Role** where **Part Templates** is checked.  
    
    ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/732e3c57-81f3-4146-a774-8c4f0deabb93)
    
6.  **Filter Properties** - Search for any part of the Name or Value to filter the list of properties.
    
    1.  The search value will be retained when selecting other parts or assemblies within the same viewer.
        
        1.  Enter a search value (Ex. ci). With All Properties selected, the list of properties filters to those that contain the search criteria.  
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/caed31ad-23c6-4a56-9b1c-316895d3d899)
            
        2.  Select a different part. The search value is retained and the list of properties is filtered.  
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/4ef4075c-42bf-4234-bf86-688032dcfd04)
            
    2.  To clear the search field and list All Properties, do one of the following:
        
        1.  Click the **x** button within the search text box.  
            
            ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/8d0dce70-3282-4b63-84c5-fb1c1d4c10d1)
            
        2.  Or, delete the text in the search text box.
            
7.  **Properties Table**
    
    1.  **Sort Columns** \- Click the up/down arrows in the column header to sort the Name or Value column. The active sort will be highlighted darker.
        
    2.  In the Properties table above, **neither All Properties or Hide Empty Values is checked**. Therefore, the Display Template, since one exists for this template, limits the table to Size, Item Descriptions, etc.
        
    3.  In the Properties table below, **All Properties** is checked. Therefore, all part properties display in alphabetic order including properties with Empty Values.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/e4f15c43-1cb3-4a1b-a6e1-59f00fcf5b24)
        
    4.  In the Properties table below, **All Properties and Hide Empty Values are checked**. Therefore, all part properties except properties with Empty Values display in alphabetic order.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/a35c6b58-97f4-4bf6-a7fa-139452516ba1)
        
    5.  In the Properties table below, since the Display Template includes no parts to show (Visible) and since All Properties has not been checked, the Properties table displays "**No data available in table**." To display properties, click check the All Properties checkbox or Edit Display Template and show selected .properties.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/fb3c46d3-30a8-4c1c-b134-555f1bdcf843)
        
    6.  **Multiple Parts Selected** - When multiple parts are selected, the Properties panel will accommodate different and common part properties.
        
        1.  In this example, 2 parts are selected. Notice that both Part Template names display separated by a semi-colon. The value <varies> indicates the value is not the same between the selected parts.
            
    7.  If one of the part properties is editable and none of the selected parts have any values, the property will display "Empty". Editing this property will set the value for all parts selected.
        
    8.  If one of the part properties is editable and any of the selected parts has a value, the property will display "<varies>". Editing this property will set the value for all parts selected.
        
    9.  Notes that have been added to a part under Stratus tool **Display - Item Numbers** > Custom Tags > Annotation Types = Notes > Select Note display 1) in the Viewer, 2) in the part's Properties under Stratus.Part.Notes, and 3) in the Notes tab.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/21bb795a-8d66-4067-87e6-f4f5dc43f2fc)
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/969c740f-f52f-42f7-915e-ccda3a42982c)
        
        1.  Notes can be removed from 1) the Viewer and 2) the part's Properties by selecting the part in the Viewer, locating the Stratus.Part.Notes property, and clicking the **REMOVE** button. **Note**: The note will still display on the Notes tab.
            
    10.  If a property displays a value, it indicates that all selected properties have the same property value. Otherwise, the property will indicate <varies>.
        
    11.  **Assembly Selected** - When an assembly is selected a Properties panel similar to the following will display.
        
        1.  All Properties Unchecked with Display Template (left); All Properties checked (right)
            

See the Assemblies > Viewer [**Display Tags and Item Numbers Toolbar**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Display-Tags-and-Item-Numbers-Toolbar "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/8749081/Assemblies+Viewer#Display-Tags-and-Item-Numbers-Toolbar") article for more information.

Note: If configured by the Administrator, Package tags may display in this viewer.

When a selection is made within the Stratus toolbar tools **Filter** or **Display Mode,** when the tool is closed, its toolbar icon will remain green to indicate that the view has been impacted by a selection. Below are the different icon color differences depending on the actions taken by the user.

1.  The toolbar icon will be inactive (white icon background) when:
    
    1.  The **tool is closed** and no selection has been made.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/8e7fc0de-2f3b-4ab8-bd13-aa113cd5e784)
        
2.  The toolbar icon will be active (blue icon background) when:
    
    1.  The **tool is open** but no selection within the tool has been made.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/23a5929d-cfc5-494e-bf9d-106482c53899)
        
    2.  The **tool is open** and a selection within the tool has been made.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/96837c9e-8e46-458b-9436-21d14b5091b9)
        
3.  With the selection made in step 2 (above) still active, the toolbar icon will be active (green icon background) when:
    
    1.  The tool is **closed and a selection within the tool was made.**  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/1a09e3a7-8dee-49ad-b43c-3986b2088f85)
        
    2.  **Note**: The green icon will turn to the blue icon when hovering over the green icon.  
        
        ![](blob:https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/00457f49-3e87-44e9-bc51-acb8e065d478)
        
4.  After the viewer page is refreshed:
    
    1.  **Display Modes** - The toolbar icon will always be inactive (white icon background).
        
    2.  **Filters** - The toolbar icon color is dependent on whether or not the last saved Filter settings are automatically applied. These settings are located under Account Settings > Profile for **Apply last session Model filter settings on load** and/or **Apply last session Package filter settings on load**. See the [**Filter Loading from Saved Settings**](https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/9043969/Models+Viewer?src=search#ModelsViewer-FilterLoadingfromSavedSettings "https://gtpservices.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SK/pages/9043969/Models+Viewer?src=search#ModelsViewer-FilterLoadingfromSavedSettings") article for more information.
        
        1.  **Checked** \- When checked the previously saved Filter settings will be checked and the toolbar icon will be active (green icon background).
            
        2.  **Unchecked** - When unchecked, no Filters will be checked after a page refresh, therefore the toolbar icon will be inactive (white icon background).
